Gold and Silver 84

▲ London Gold Price: Today (29th), the London gold price is 135 shillings and 5.5 pence, down 9.5 pence from yesterday.

▲ London Silver Bar: Today (29th), the London silver price rose by 0.0625. The spot price is 19 shillings and 9.375 pence, and the futures price is 20 shillings. Speculators bought in the morning, there were few transactions, and the closing was stable.

▲ New York Silver Bar: Today (29th) telegram, President Roosevelt's veto of the soldiers' pension bill has now been overturned by Congress, causing the silver price to open firmly. At the same time, foreign news is also favorable to the silver market, and sentiment still tends to be bullish. However, merchants are still awaiting news from Washington and the Secretary of the Treasury's opinion on the Dies silver bill. Therefore, the silver futures market opened with gains ranging from 37 to 55 pounds sterling higher than yesterday's close.

▲ Bombay Silver Bar: The Bombay silver market closed silently today (29th), with the price falling by four annas. The spot price is 54 rupees and 11 annas.

Exchange Rates 85

▲ British-American Exchange Rate: In today's (29th) London foreign exchange market, the pound sterling is quite firm, because the UK's income, apart from expenditures, has a considerable surplus, and there are now fears of inflation in the United States. The British-American exchange rate opened at 5 dollars, 1 dime, and 1.25 cents, the same as yesterday's close. The price then rose, once reaching 5 dollars, 1 dime, and 4.5 cents, but the latest price is 5 dollars, 1 dime, and 3.75 cents. Also, one US dollar equals 3 shillings, 10 pence, and 7.15 British pence.

▲ British-French Exchange Rate: Today's (29th) telegram, there is a risk of renewed political turmoil in France, so the franc is weak. The British-French exchange rate opened at 77 francs 68, up nine pounds sterling from yesterday's close. At 2:00 PM, it was 78 francs 09, 41 pounds sterling higher than this morning's opening.

▲ US-British Exchange Rate: The New York exchange rate for British currency closed at 5.1125 on the previous day. Today's opening prices were: First session 5.1350, Second session 5.125, Third session 5.125, Fourth session 5.125, Fifth session 5.125, Sixth session 5.125.

▲ US-French Exchange Rate: Today's (29th) telegram, the US-French exchange rate opened at 6.58.

Cotton and Wheat 86

▲ New York Cotton: Today (29th), sentiment in the cotton market was mixed. Bankers and merchants bought in, and bulls also covered, so the scattered selling was absorbed, and the market price rose slightly. Subsequently, due to the possibility of inflation, the opening gains were able to develop. However, since it is the holiday season, trading is not strong.

▲ Bombay Cotton: Today (29th), the Bombay cotton market fell due to the closing of long positions, but later rebounded slightly due to speculative buying. The closing price for white Luoqu cotton for April-May delivery was 194 rupees, down 1.5 rupees.

▲ Liverpool Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was quiet today (29th). At 1:00 PM, the price for July delivery was 6.03, down three pounds sterling from yesterday.

▲ Liverpool Wheat: Today (29th), the Liverpool wheat market was more stable than yesterday. The price for July delivery rose by 125 to 4 shillings and 5.375 pence.

The Xiao and Gao Bandits Will Soon Be Eliminated 94

(Changsha) At the expanded memorial week yesterday, He Jian reported on the bandit situation, stating that the Xiao and Gao bandits originally had over ten thousand men and about six to seven thousand guns. After two months of relentless pursuit, they have been repeatedly attacked and are in a state of utter disarray, having exhausted their ammunition. Currently, the Gao bandits have only about seven to eight hundred guns left, and the Xiao bandits have only a little over a thousand. Many officers and soldiers of the pseudo-regiments and companies have surrendered in recent days. In the past half-month, it has been reported that our army has captured about eight to nine hundred bandit guns, and local militias and volunteer corps have captured about a thousand bandit guns. Most of the remaining guns have been lost, scattered along the way, or buried by the bandits in various places. Orders have now been given to all armies to thoroughly search to prevent harm to the local population. The Xiao and Gao bandits will soon be completely eliminated. (Central News Agency dispatch, 27th)

Flash Floods in the Upper Reaches of the Qiantang River 95

(Hangzhou) Zhejiang has experienced continuous rain and snow. Flash floods have occurred in the upper reaches of the Qiantang River, and the main lines of the Jiangguang, Changyu, Yulan, Longjin, and Li highways have all been damaged, disrupting traffic. (Central News Agency dispatch, 29th)

Northern Route Army

Recapture of Guihua City 96

=Bandits Retreat towards Jianning and Qingliu=

=Northeast Two Routes Advance Towards Western Fujian=

Nanchang Correspondence: After the 3rd and 6th Routes of the Jiangxi Northeast Route Army and the Fujian Northern Bandit Suppression Army recovered the counties of Shaxian, Yong'an, Jiangle, Shunchang, and Taining, they continued to advance towards Guihua, Qingliu, and Jianning to suppress bandits. The goal is to clear out the red bandits in northern Fujian in the shortest possible time, complete the blockade line and defense arrangements between eastern Jiangxi and northern Fujian, and then, together with the Southern Route Army, launch a three-pronged attack on the pseudo-central areas of Tingzhou, Liancheng, Ruijin, and Huichang. According to front-line news from the Northern Route Army, certain units of the National Army attacked and advanced from Jiangle and Shunchang towards Guihua. The pseudo 7th Army Corps, 19th Division, and the Independent 7th Division in Guihua City, due to the rapid advance of the main force of the National Army and the presence of the National Army stationed in Jiangshunyongsha, which formed a tripod with Guihua, feared being surrounded. Starting from the 22nd, they began to retreat towards Jianning and Qingliu, leaving only a part to fight against the National Army in the Longhu area northeast of Guihua to cover their retreat. On the morning of the 23rd, a certain division advanced from Tiecenguan to Longhu and engaged in battle with about a thousand bandits. The bandits fought and retreated. At noon, the National Army recovered Guihua City, and the remaining bandits fled west of Guihua to join the bandits retreating to Jianning and Qingliu. After the division entered the city, in addition to leaving a part to defend the city, another part advanced westward, had passed Lintuo, and reported the situation of the recapture of Guihua to the headquarters on the 23rd. It is said that after the recapture of Guihua, Jianning was surrounded by the Northeast Two Route Armies, and the recapture is also not a problem. (March 25th)

Han Fuju Organizes

Six Columns to Suppress Liu's Bandits 97

=Han Personally Assumes Command and First Column=

=Issues Proclamation Offering Reward of 10,000 Yuan for the Capture of Liu's Bandits=

Jinan Correspondence: After Liu Guitang's remnants crossed the Jinpu Railway near Wandeful on the 24th, they took the road to Laiwu and Xintai, fleeing towards Mount Meng in the hope of returning to their old lair at Baodugu. According to official reports, Liu's bandits reached the Laiwu county border on the 25th, numbering about seven to eight hundred. Zhan Shutang's unit, Yun Qichang's brigade, and the 74th Division, Ma Guanyi's brigade, are in hot pursuit. Xie Shuxian, commander of the Southern Shandong militia, also led his troops overnight to Mengyin to intercept them. He also ordered the militia joint defense associations of Xintai, Laiwu, Mengyin, Sishui, Tai'an, and other counties to mobilize and intercept them. The scattered bandits in western Shandong, Feicheng, Wenshang, and Dongping are being cleared by the militias of the respective counties. Sun Tongxuan, commander of the 20th Division, came to Jinan from Yanzhou on the afternoon of the 25th to meet Han and report on the bandit suppression process. In order to thoroughly eliminate Liu's bandits, Han decided to launch a large-scale encirclement. He summoned Sun Tongxuan, Gu Liangmin, Liu Shuxiang, and others to discuss and determine a concrete plan to eliminate Liu's bandits, which mainly involved drawing eighteen regiments from various divisions, dividing them into four directions to suppress them, forming six columns, each with a commander and three regiments. Han himself assumed the position of commander-in-chief of the bandit suppression army and commander of the first column. Sun Tongxuan was appointed commander of the second column, Cao Fulin was appointed commander of the third column, Gu Liangmin was appointed commander of the fourth column, Li Hanzhang was appointed commander of the fifth column, and Zhan Shutang was appointed commander of the sixth column. The bandit suppression armies from each direction were scheduled to depart from the Jinpu and Jiaoji railways to their destinations on a specified date, awaiting the order for a general offensive. It is rumored that Sun Tongxuan is advancing east from Yanzhou, Zhan Shutang is advancing east from Tai'an, Cao Fulin is advancing south from Boshan, Li Hanzhang is advancing southwest from Ju County and Zhucheng, Gu Liangmin is advancing north from Zaozhuang and Linyi, and Han himself will lead troops south from Weixian, forming a large encirclement. It is expected that Liu's bandits can be wiped out in the shortest possible time. At 9:10 PM on the 25th, Gu Liangmin left Jinan and led his troops forward. Cao Fulin led his troops south from the Jiaoji Railway nearby. Sun Tongxuan was also scheduled to return to Yanzhou on the 26th to lead his troops to suppress the bandits. Han Fuju will first go east to a certain place in the coming days and then turn south to supervise the suppression. According to Gu Liangmin when he left Jinan at the station, this time Liu's bandits infiltrated Shandong Province. I led the direct subordinate units of the division headquarters and Ning Chunxiao's unit of the 64th Brigade, together with Sun Xuefa's regiment of the 20th Division of Commander Sun, Jiang Boyuan's regiment of the 74th Division, Li Xuande's cavalry regiment, and Gu Liangyou's militia of the 3rd Route, and Xie Shuxian's militia of the 4th Route, to track and encircle the bandits, and engaged in five fierce battles with them. The first time was at Longguji and Taipingji in Juye, the second time was at Dinglichang (Zhuangmin) (Liuguantun) in Yuncheng, the third time was at Jinkou in Dongping, the fourth time was at Daxiaokaoshan in Feicheng, and the fifth time was near Huangshan in Jieshou, especially the battle at Kaoshan was the most intense. The number of bandits originally reached three thousand, and after several fierce attacks, the casualties were definitely not small, and most of them were defeated. The remaining bandits, who fled east across the Jinpu Railway, were no more than five or six hundred, already in Laiwu, etc.

Liu Jin, the magistrate of Feicheng County, reported to Han Fuju, chairman of the provincial government, on the 25th that Liu Guitang had been bombed to death during the fierce battle in Feicheng. Other sources have no definite proof. It is also heard that Han Fuju has separately telegraphed the Central Government and Chairman Jiang of Nanchang, and Minister He of the Beiping Ministry of Military Affairs for verification of the daily bandit suppression process and future elimination plans.

Also, according to news received by the headquarters this morning (26th), the remnants of Liu's bandits have now fled to the Luxi Town area in the northeast Laiwu territory of Tai'an and continue to flee. The number is only seven to eight hundred, and there are no more than three to four hundred guns. Yun Qichang's brigade and Ma Guanyi's brigade are working hard to pursue them. The captured bandits were sent to Jinan for interrogation and were mostly from the Northeast. They said that Liu Guitang himself wore a gray cotton robe and brought two yellow horses, alternating riding them, and was extremely fierce. Han launched a large-scale encirclement and suppression of Liu's bandits, starting today, and specially stipulated the temporary regulations for bandit suppression: those who capture Liu Guitang will be rewarded with 10,000 yuan in foreign currency, and those who kill him will be rewarded with 6,000 yuan in foreign currency. On the one hand, a notice was also prepared and sent to various counties for posting. The notice reads, "It has been found that Liu Guitang was previously entrenched in Nanshan, burning, killing, and looting, and the local area was devastated. This chairman cherishes the people and sent a large army to severely suppress him, and then took the power to appease him, hoping that he would repent and do good. However, the bandit's ambitions are difficult to tame, and he rebelled and fled without reason, disturbing several provinces. He has always been like a rebel, and recently led bandits from outside the Guan to return to southern Shandong. I mourn for my fathers, elders, brothers, and sisters, who will inevitably suffer further destruction. I am willing to lead the military and civilians of the entire province to rise up and suppress the bandits. The orders are strict, and military law is strict. In addition to ordering all armies to strictly abide by military discipline and love the local area, six articles of the temporary regulations for bandit suppression are hereby promulgated, which should be strictly followed. This notice." Temporary regulations for bandit suppression: (1) Those who kill Liu Guitang will be awarded 6,000 yuan in foreign currency, and those who capture him alive will be awarded 10,000 yuan. (2) Those who achieve outstanding results in bandit suppression will be heavily rewarded. (3) Those who seize bandit weapons will be heavily rewarded. (4) Those who protect villages or report accurate bandit information will be appropriately rewarded. (5) Those who supply the bandits with weapons, ammunition, food, or those whose guns are seized by the bandits and fail to prevent it will be severely punished. (6) Those who collude with bandits, harbor bandits, or delay reporting bandit information, or even abandon cities and villages, will be held jointly liable, and the heads of the township, district, town, and county will be punished. Han also issued an order to all subordinate troops to print and distribute seven articles of the temporary regulations for bandit suppression: (1) Strictly obey orders, earnestly suppress bandits, and those who achieve outstanding results will be heavily rewarded. (2) Those who capture Liu Guitang will be awarded 10,000 yuan in foreign currency, and those who kill him will be awarded 6,000 yuan. (3) Those who seize a large number of bandit weapons will be heavily rewarded. (4) Those who linger and fail to advance, delay military opportunities, or withdraw without authorization in violation of orders will be severely punished. (5) Those who disturb the local area or demand supplies without paying will be severely punished. (6) Those who leak military secrets will be severely punished. (7) Those who corrupt military discipline and morality will be severely punished. For the above seven articles, rewards and punishments for senior officers will be determined by the commander-in-chief, and for junior officers, the respective commanders will report for approval at any time. (26th)

Henan Bandits Wang and Ma

Join Forces to Attack Ye County 98

The County Government Has Already Deployed Militia to Defend the City

Zhang Fang Will Go to Nanyang to Supervise the Suppression

Kaifeng Correspondence: Western and southern Henan have always been areas where bandits are rampant. A month ago, after Liu Guitang's bandit unit crossed the Yellow River and fled, Wang You's unit of more than two thousand men also fled back to Lushi and Song County from the Shangnan area of Shaanxi. Ma Xiyou, Xiao Liushao, Fang Dashen, and other units roamed the Deng County and Neixiang areas. South of the Yellow River, there were traces of bandits everywhere. Later, Liu Guitang's bandit unit was driven out of Henan, and Wang You's unit was also almost completely wiped out by Zhang Fang's unit of the 20th Route Army. Ma, Xiao, Fang, and others fled into Yunyang in northern Hubei. The bandit problem in Zhongzhou seemed to be on the verge of being resolved. Unexpectedly, recently, Shi Jianbin, Tu Laiyuan, and other units of more than seven hundred men have re-disturbed the Zhengyang and Xi County areas, and incidents of kidnapping occur every day. Ma Xiyou, Wang You, Xiao Liushao, Fang Dashen, and other units have also returned to Wan County. Zhang Fang telegraphed Bian on the 25th, stating that according to a telephone report from Wang Tuanfu of the 457th Regiment, Ma, Wang, and other bandits had infiltrated the area east of Caodian in the east of the county at 10:00 PM on the 24th. His regiment launched a night attack, killing dozens of bandits and capturing several rifles. One officer and fourteen soldiers of his regiment were wounded or killed. After being attacked, the bandits split into two groups, one fleeing northwest and the other fleeing east. He is currently pursuing them, and he will personally go to supervise the suppression within days to ensure their annihilation. Also, a Ye County dispatch stated that Wang You and Ma Xiyou joined forces, leading about three thousand bandits, and fled north from Fangcheng to the Xiaobao'an area, more than fifty miles south of the city, plotting to disturb the old county, thirty miles from the city. After being blocked by the 3rd Squadron of the Baoan and the Strongman Team, they turned east, detoured north, and showed a tendency to attack the city. In addition to the artillery battalion of the 20th Route Army and the Baoan Team stationed in the city, the county government feared that the strength was insufficient and has transferred several hundred militiamen from the 1st and 5th districts to defend the city and assist in the defense. (March 27th)

Severe Storm Re-Attacks Wuhan 99

=Accompanied by Thunder and Rain=

=Followed by Spring Snow=

Hankou Correspondence: Since the two earthquakes in Wuhan on the 18th, followed by a violent hurricane on the 20th, the climate has been unusually changeable. When it is hot, people feel that wearing a lined coat is too much, and when it is cold, even heavy fur coats are not warm enough. On the evening of the 27th, thunder was first heard, shaking the roofs. At that time, the sky and earth were dark, and the rain poured down. The low-lying streets and alleys were deeply flooded. At 11:00 PM, the storm struck again, blowing off tiles, destroying houses, and causing sand and stones to fly. The intensity was as fierce as the hurricane on the 20th. The city's electricity was cut off more than ten times, and telegraph and telephone services were also mostly interrupted. After 3:00 AM on the 28th, it gradually subsided. At dawn, heavy spring snow fell, and it was even worse at noon. Large snowflakes flew around, as big as palms. The indoor temperature dropped to 48 degrees Fahrenheit, as if it were midwinter. It is said that a giant thunder on the 27th struck a large ancient tree on Black Mountain in Hanyang, which was ten times as thick as a hug. A giant snake inside was also electrocuted. The storm also destroyed many houses. A large number of wooden boards were found on the river surface, which seemed to be ship materials, suggesting that there must have been many shipwrecks in the upper reaches of the Xiang River. (28th)

Page 9

Reporter Inspection Team

Arrives in Kangding from Ya'an 100

Crossing High Snow-Covered Mountains

People Eagerly Await Central Government's Attention to National Defense

Ya'an, February 26th: Departing from Ya'an to Western Sichuan for inspection, sometimes using sedan chairs, which served as embellishments on the long journey. The only other figures on the long road are a few farmers carrying goods and the coolies carrying tea. Regarding the tea carriers, men, women, old, and young are all involved. The amount carried depends on their strength. The maximum is thirteen packages, each weighing seventeen catties, totaling 221 catties. They rest every few dozen steps to conquer this long journey of thousands of miles. The inconvenience of transportation, the difficulty of transport, and the suffering of the people can be imagined. On the same day, they traveled eighty miles and arrived at Rongjing County. The county is named after the Rong River and the Jing River, and its area is sixty miles east to west and one hundred sixty miles north to south. It is rich in copper, iron, and coal mines, but agricultural production is insufficient. There is only one high school for boys and one for girls in the county seat, and education is not very developed. On the 27th, they traveled from Rongjing to Huangyibao for rest, only forty miles, because from here they had to climb the Daxiangling, which required a day's work, so they had to spend the night at the foot of the mountain. However, even at the foot of the mountain, the altitude was already 1,400 meters (above sea level). On the morning of the 28th, at 6:00 AM, they went to Huangyibao and braved the rain to climb Daxiangling, a mountain road of forty-five miles. After traveling ten miles, the rain turned into snow, and the accumulated snow became higher and thicker, and the temperature became lower. In a silver world, everything was white. In order to travel faster, the reporter gave up the sedan chair and walked, feeling warm due to the effort, and not fearing the ice and snow. At 2:00 PM, they reached the highest peak, called Caoxieping, and turned downhill. The road was steep and narrow, so it was shortened to fifteen miles. The accumulated snow turned into icy scales, and they fell and got up again, rushing down. After traveling another five miles, they arrived at Hanyuan County. The wind was strong, worthy of the name Qingfeng Ya Yu (Clear Wind and Elegant Rain). (Hanyuan was originally called Qingxi.) Having crossed this 2,900-meter-high Daxiangling, they did it in one go, so it was still early. After a brief meal, they continued their journey, traveling another twenty-five miles to Hanyuanchang for accommodation. This market town is the largest in Hanyuan County. Because its trade is closer to Western Sichuan, the market is bustling and commerce is prosperous. The Hanyuan essence is gathered here. A middle school is also located in this market town. There are four high schools in the county, and education is relatively developed. On March 1st, due to the fatigue of the porters, they rested in Hanyuanchang to regain their strength. On the 2nd, they left the market town and traveled seventy-five miles to Datouzhen. This place is the ancient Feiyue County, located at the foot of the Feiyue Ridge. The land is barren, the people are poor, and the population is sparse. In the Qing Dynasty, the county was abolished and turned into a town. After the restoration, it was changed to a sub-county, belonging to Hanyuan, and a county assistant administrative office was established to handle local affairs. They went to bed early that day and set off early on the morning of the 3rd, climbing Feiyue Ridge again. The ice, snow, and climate of this mountain were no less than those of Daxiangling, but there were more mountain paths, making it easier to walk. Reaching its peak at 2,910 meters, it was ten meters higher than Daxiangling. The boundary between Sichuan and Western Sichuan Provinces is divided by this mountain. Going down the mountain from here to the west, they entered Western Sichuan Province. They rested at Hualinping at the foot of the mountain, a sub-county of Luding County. There is also a county assistant office. The population is very small, with only dozens of households in the entire town and only a few hundred households in the entire township. On the 4th, they traveled dozens of miles and arrived at Luding County, the easternmost county in Western Sichuan. From Hualinping to Luding County, the barren mountains stretched endlessly, the soil was dry and loose, and the grass was withered and the trees were sparse, which was completely different from the land of Sichuan Province. However, the mountain range formation contains a lot of minerals, but unfortunately no one pays attention to it. The county covers an area of 120 miles from north to south, and is narrower from east to west. The population is four thousand households, with more than 30,000 people. There are three high schools and one normal school. The main product is medicinal materials, and very little farmland has been reclaimed. Fifty miles from the city, Lengqi has a hundred acres of flat land, which is the largest farmland in the county. However, nineteen percent of the property rights are illegally occupied by French Catholic priests. The Catholic Church is outside the county seat, with tall foreign buildings, and its power can manipulate the rural economy of the entire county and control officials and people. On the 5th, they left Luding City, crossed the iron-linked suspension bridge, crossed the Luding River (formerly known as Xiaojin River), traveled sixty miles, and rested at Wasigou. On the 6th, they traveled another sixty miles and arrived in Kangding at around 4:00 PM. After entering the city, there were slogans all over the street, earnestly requesting the central government to resolve the Kang Tibetan disputes, and eagerly hoping that the financial and industrial circles would develop the treasures of Western Sichuan. The authorities chose the office of the Panchen Lama in Xijing as a reception center. Tang Ying, commander of the Xijing Tuntian, and Deng Xiang, brigade commander of the Sichuan-Western Sichuan border defense army, came to visit and reported in detail the truth about the Kang Tibetan military disputes and the tragic situation on the front line. These national defense soldiers, in the icy and snowy weather, lacked food, ammunition, and clothing, and resisted the Tibetan army. Many died in the war due to hunger and cold. It was tragic to hear. Also, the rear soldiers seen in the Kangding market were also very pitiful in their hunger and cold. During their six-day stay in Kangding, in addition to holding meetings to welcome them, private visits by people from various agencies, legal groups, gentry, merchants, and civilians were also numerous. They all eagerly hoped that the central government and the people of the country would pay attention to the national defense and development of Western Sichuan as soon as possible. Also, because Kangding is inhabited by both Han and Tibetan people, the educated people of Western Sichuan and Tibetans living in Kangding also came to welcome them, hoping that the people of the whole country would help. On the 13th, they left Kangding and returned east. On the 16th, they arrived at Huayang. According to the original plan, they began to return to Ya'an along the new road at Hualinping. This road was newly opened and completed, except for crossing a mountain near Hualinping, it can bypass the high mountains of Feiyue and Daxiangling, and the road is flat and the scenery is beautiful. Once this road is completed, it will be very convenient for those entering Western Sichuan in the future, as they will not have to trek through the two high mountains that pierce the clouds. Also, traveling along the new road takes six days, saving two days compared to the old road. On the 19th, they returned to Ya'an and decided to take a bamboo raft along the Ya River to Jiajiang on the 21st, climb Mount Emei, transfer to Jiading, follow the upper reaches of the Yangtze River downstream, and return to Chongqing via Xufu, Luzhou, Hejiang, and Jiangjin to inspect the situation in southern Sichuan. (Guowen News Agency)

Wuxi 101

The Court Issued Summonses Twice

Gu Renfa Expressed Willingness to Appear in Court

The case of the former Chief of the Second Public Security Bureau, Liu Zhuomin, and his wife, Wen Rongzhen, resisting transfer and obstructing official duties, and involving the wife of the Director of Civil Affairs, Gu Renfa, and her daughter, Li Shuyun, being detained by the local county court, has been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. It is now known that the county court has issued summonses twice, ordering Gu Renfa to appear in court for questioning. More than twenty women from this county, including Zhang He and Xu Deyin, expressed indignation at Li Shuyun's arrest and jointly sent a letter of condolence to Li Shuyun. The details are recorded separately below.

The Department of Civil Affairs Submitted Eight Pieces of Evidence After the Li Shuyun case occurred, the Director of Civil Affairs, Gu Renfa, believed that Li Shuyun's crimes were related to the national principles. If national laws could not be applied to close relatives, how could officials be rectified and examples set for subordinates? Therefore, he telegraphed Chairman Chen of the Provincial Government, requesting punishment. The original telegram stated: "If I do not abide by national laws, how can I govern the people? The law should not spare relatives; let me be the first to abide by it. Lax family governance is inexcusable." Yesterday, Director Gu collected eight pieces of evidence related to the Li Shuyun case and submitted them to the Provincial Government for transfer to the local county court for investigation.

Gu Renfa Decided to Obey the Summons and Appear in Court The Procuratorate of the local county court previously telegraphed Gu Renfa to appear in court for questioning. However, Gu had gone to Jiangxi and had not returned, so he could not come to Wuxi. The Provincial Government replied with a telegram to inform them of the situation. Now, the Procuratorate has learned that Gu has returned to the province, so yesterday, they issued a summons for the second time, ordering Gu Renfa to appear in court for questioning. It is heard that the summons will be delivered today. Director Gu Renfa stated that the case must be handled according to judicial procedures. If it is legally required for him to appear in court, he will immediately go to Wuxi. Therefore, it is expected that the Director may obey the summons and surrender himself.

The Department of Civil Affairs Issued a Strange Letter The other day, Director Gu used the Department of Civil Affairs' Order No. 3 to instruct the local county government to forward it to the county court. The content mentioned a letter to Director Gu, signed by Wu Chahua, Zhou Zhengwu, and Chen Jianzhi, recounting Li Shuyun's background, which was described as very humble and sordid. It also stated that Li Fengqi, a member of Li Shuyun's clan, was originally in the countryside, acting as a guarantor and gentry, but had no knowledge. He spent 700 yuan to seek a position as Chief of Public Security Bureau, etc. Upon inspection of the original letter, there were many doubts. It cannot be determined whether Wu Zonghua and others are real people. However, Director Gu's willingness to marry this Li Shuyun is even more suspicious. Now, the local county government, upon receiving the order, has forwarded it to the county court's Procuratorate for verification.

The County Public Security Bureau Hosted Reporters Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, the Director of the local county Public Security Bureau, the Director of Academic Affairs of the Police Training School, Yu Die'ao, and Inspector Huang Bingnan, hosted a conversation with correspondents from various newspapers at the Washington Hotel. Huang Bingnan distributed a passage of Director Gu's speech that had been printed. He said that this text was sent to Wuxi this morning by a special envoy from the Department of Civil Affairs and delivered to the Department of Civil Affairs inspector in Wuxi, Zeng Binqiu, who instructed them to forward it. He also repeatedly emphasized that the Liu Zhuomin resistance case and the marriage dispute between Gu and Li were two completely separate matters and should not be linked in the reports. Subsequently, Yu and Huang hosted a Western-style meal at the hotel's Western restaurant, and the guests and hosts parted on happy terms.

Li Will Present a Defense Against the Statement Yesterday (29th) at 5:00 PM, reporters visited the detention center to inquire about her condition. According to the doctor who examined Li Shuyun, Li Shuyun's condition had improved compared to the previous day. She ate some rice porridge, but she still did not feel hungry. In the morning, Li also vomited a small amount of fresh blood. Li stated that she intended to present a defense against the statement published by Gu Renfa.

Tax Evasion Case Trial 102

Xu Jigong, the director of the local slaughter tax collection office, passed away a long time ago. Now, two important staff members of the office, Lian Shaoshan and Gu Yunpeng, are secretly acting as agents. Lian and Gu have been embezzling funds, totaling five or six thousand yuan. The details are recorded below: (1) The supplementary tax collection for three and a half months from June to September of the 21st year actually received around 12,000 yuan. However, Lian and others reported the amount to the Provincial Education Funding Management Office as 8,708 yuan, and later reported that only 6,785.77 yuan was received. The embezzlement amounted to around 4,000 yuan. (2) The local education surcharge was more than 2,400 yuan, but Lian and others only remitted more than 1,000 yuan, embezzling more than 1,000 yuan. (3) The local construction surcharge was more than 1,200 yuan, but Lian and others only remitted more than 500 yuan, embezzling more than 500 yuan. In total, the embezzlement amounted to more than 5,000 yuan. A local resident, Mao Jinshan, filed a complaint with the county court's Procuratorate. Yesterday was the court hearing, but Lian and Gu did not appear in court. Mao Jinshan requested that they be arrested and brought to justice. The prosecutor in charge approved the request and adjourned the court. It is also heard that the county education bureau has ordered the office to remit the short-paid funds to the bureau by a specific date. If there is further delay, they will present the case to the county for arrest and pursuit, to safeguard education funds and emphasize public funds.

Changzhou

Pawn Industry Opposes Shanghai Bank Operating Pawnshops 103

Zhang Peishen, chairman of the Wuyi Pawn Industry Association, and others stated that according to newspaper reports, the Shanghai Bank's new plan to regulate agricultural finance this year intends to establish farmers' mortgage loan institutions similar to pawnshops. In addition to mortgaging agricultural products, clothes, jewelry, and utensils can also be pawned, so that farmers can borrow small amounts of money at low interest rates whenever they need it. Trial operations are already underway in Jiangning and Dongtai, and it is planned to gradually promote them in the future. They believe that this will hinder the pawn industry and cut off the livelihoods of workers. They have drafted relief measures and sent a letter to the Jiangsu Provincial Pawn Industry Federation, requesting that it be submitted to the general meeting for discussion and resolution on April 16th. Yesterday (28th), they also sent letters to the pawn industry associations in various counties, urging them to unite and fight together. At that time, representatives will be sent to attend, jointly appeal, and maintain the industry.

Spring Cold and Snowfall 104

Since the beginning of spring, the climate here has warmed up suddenly, and the highest temperature has reached 72 degrees Fahrenheit. Unexpectedly, it has suddenly turned cold in recent days, with continuous rain. On the morning of the 28th, snowflakes fluttered and the temperature dropped sharply to 38 degrees. People put on fur coats again. The spring harvest will be affected.

Four New District Chiefs Announced 105

The local autonomous administrative region was originally divided into fifteen districts. Now, according to provincial orders, in order to save expenses, it has been merged into eight districts. The boundaries of each district have now been redefined and will be implemented on April 1st. All the old district offices will be closed by the end of March. The selection of district chiefs will be made from the original fifteen people, strictly selected, and submitted by the county to the province for approval. News has been received from the province that four people have been announced first. The first district chief is Shen Changjun, the second district chief is Lu Wanrong, the fifth district chief is Xu Jingyu, and the seventh district chief is Zhu Qingnan. The remaining four are still under consideration.

Tax Police Harassment Arouses Public Outrage 106

Yang, the captain of the third detachment of the Haining tax police, stationed at Xiaoputuo in Haining, usually condoned his subordinates to harass people everywhere in the name of searching for smuggled salt. They privately took chickens and ducks from villagers and moved objects, which they sold in the Dadongmen area. Local people have complained. Recently, the Chunxi Town Office in the first district of Haining organized the screening of a movie to raise funds for road repairs. The detachment leader, along with many relatives and friends, went to watch the movie the other day. They were wearing uniforms and had no badges. They forcibly wanted to enter but were unsuccessful. They rushed back to the detachment headquarters and led the entire tax police force to swarm the area. They first opened the gate and ordered people to be beaten upon sight and objects to be destroyed upon touch. The order was disrupted, and countless viewers were trampled and injured. Among those beaten and injured by the tax police were Qian Yueqing, the secretary of the chamber of commerce, and Huang Tinggui, the ticket seller. Their heads were broken and bleeding, and their injuries were severe. They have now filed a lawsuit with the county court for injury verification. Local legal organizations, believing that the detachment leader was so barbaric and harassed the people, were extremely indignant. The Haining County Chamber of Commerce, Property Association, Women's Association, and other legal organizations have telegraphed Chairman Lu of the Provincial Government, Director Feng, and Team Leader Zhang, requesting severe punishment according to law to ensure local peace and uphold the law. It is heard that Director Feng has sent someone to investigate the truth and take action accordingly.

Team leader Hu Feiqian, along with members Li Zhankui and others, and the Public Security Bureau's wooden gun team, went to the house that night to search, but there was no trace of the bandits.

Special Article

On the Draft Constitution (Continued) (Zhang Yuanruo) 108

(5) The National Assembly

(1) In critiquing this chapter, there is a crucial premise that cannot be ignored: is the National Assembly a constitution-making body (PruvoivConstitucot) or an organ generated based on the constitution (PruvoivConstitucotc)? Article 51, Paragraph 4 of the draft constitution stipulates the "formulation" of the constitution, indicating it is a constitution-making body. Therefore, its existence should precede the constitution. However, other articles indicate that its organization and functions are all defined by the constitution, suggesting it is generated by the constitution and its existence should follow the constitution. How should we interpret this contradiction? To resolve it, the constitution should either not include provisions on the organization and functions of the National Assembly, or delete the word "formulation" in Article 51, Paragraph 4. One of these must be chosen for consistency in legal principles and facts.

(2) Regarding the organization of the National Assembly in Article 47, we find four unsatisfactory points: 1. The electoral system still suffers from the drawbacks of the traditional representative system, making it too outdated. This extreme form of localism is not only out of step with the times but also makes it difficult to select true talent. 2. The population of each county varies, but each elects one representative, which is unfair. Moreover, the number of counties in our country is not small, resulting in too many representatives, causing many obstacles. The division of electoral districts in other countries does not entirely use existing administrative districts as a standard. To correct this, refer to Chapter 10 of the Russian Constitution (Note 6). 3. After representatives are elected, if they are unqualified or incompetent, they should be subject to recall by the people. The constitution does not provide for this, so it should be supplemented. 4. National representatives bear significant responsibilities and sacred missions, but the only qualification restriction is age, which seems too superficial.

(3) Since the National Assembly is based on Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings, it should be clearly defined as the highest organ exercising the power of governance. However, the functions prescribed in Article 51 do not fully align with this purpose. This is one contradiction. According to Article 69 in Chapter 7, the President and the five Yuan are responsible to the National Assembly. However, the Assembly lacks provisions on budget approval, votes of confidence, policy inquiries, and recognition or ratification of war and peace, and amnesty. How can the Assembly exercise its power to supervise the government, and how can the government be held accountable to the Assembly? This is another contradiction. Furthermore, the number of attendees and voting requirements for the Assembly are not specified, suggesting a neglect of national affairs.

(4) Moreover, the use of the veto power has no precedent in our country, and the people lack experience in it. The constitution lacks detailed regulations on the methods, procedures, and scope of application of the veto power, which will create difficulties in its application in the future. This should be noted and supplemented in advance. With the National Assembly meeting only once every three years, this veto power will not only be insufficient to remedy legislative tyranny but will also be equivalent to a mere formality. A way to correct this should be sought.

(5) The establishment of the National Committee is a good idea and a practical provision tailored to local conditions. Given China's vast territory, large population, and the public's limited political knowledge and capabilities, the National Assembly may become unwieldy. However, according to Article 54, the powers of the representatives of the National Assembly end on the day of adjournment. Yet, Article 55 stipulates that members of the National Committee are not limited to representatives of the National Assembly, suggesting that its organization is not sound, as it cannot fully inherit the governing power of the nation.

(6) Furthermore, Article 58 stipulates that the National Committee has more real power than the National Assembly. Entrusting such significant powers and responsibilities to such an unsound and small organization not only violates the principle of popular sovereignty but is also dangerous in practice. First, the constitution does not specify to whom the members of the National Committee should be accountable. If they abuse their powerful position and take regressive measures, there will be no recourse. Second, if there is a conflict between the powers of the Assembly and the Committee, how will it be resolved? This is also not mentioned, and it will inevitably lead to disputes in the future. It is hoped that this will be carefully considered and amended.

(6) The Division of Powers Between the Central and Local Governments

How to divide the powers between the central and local governments varies among countries around the world. Since the Republic of China, contemporary scholars have debated fiercely, advocating either centralism or provincial autonomy. The boundaries of powers have not been clearly defined, leading to frequent turmoil. Article 60 of the draft constitution reconciles these views and adopts the principle of balanced powers, in accordance with Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings. However, Dr. Sun only provided the principle of balanced powers without concrete regulations. The so-called national consistency and local adaptation are abstract and lack specificity, requiring further in-depth research.

Examining the legislative principles for dividing the powers between the central and local governments in various countries, the central government typically enumerates its powers, while the local governments have a general scope. However, the content of the central enumeration is complex, and the legislation of each country varies. The advantages and disadvantages of each system differ significantly. (1) According to the US Constitution, the powers of the central government are divided into two types: exclusive powers, which are exercised exclusively by the central government, and concurrent powers, which can be exercised by the states until the central government acts, after which state laws become invalid. The remaining unspecified powers are reserved to the states. This is a unique feature and advantage of the American system, as it allows the central government to thoroughly and effectively exercise its powers in all states, while also allowing the states to fully develop their autonomy. (2) The German Constitution enumerates the powers of the central government, distinguishing between those exercised exclusively by the central government, those belonging to the central government but exercised by the state governments on its behalf with central supervision, and those for which the central government only has supervisory power. The drawback of this system is that the central government cannot directly and effectively exercise its powers in the states. (3) The Austrian Constitution enumerates three types of powers of the central government: those for which both legislative and executive powers belong to the central government, those for which legislative power belongs to the central government and executive power belongs to the local governments, and those for which the power to set principles belongs to the central government and the power to execute and elaborate details belongs to the local governments. The drawback of this system is that the legislative and executive powers are not consistent, preventing the central government from effectively exercising its powers in the provinces, similar to the German system.

From this, we can understand the advantages and disadvantages of the various systems. However, when making our choice, we must use the historical political problems of our country and the current political needs as the standard for our selection. The most prominent defects in our country's past politics are twofold: one is that the powers of the central government cannot be thoroughly exercised at the local level, with each province acting independently and orders not leaving the capital; the other is that local autonomy has not been effectively promoted, and the people's political knowledge and capabilities have not made significant progress. Therefore, the greatest need for our country at present is to centralize power and promote decentralization, enabling the central government to thoroughly and effectively exercise its powers in all provinces to achieve national unity, while also providing constitutional guarantees for local autonomy to promote its development. This is the unique strength of the American system and the direction that our country should take at present. Evaluating today's draft constitution in this light, we believe that the provisions of Article 61 are too weak, and the matters it lists are too complex. In our view, the exclusive powers of the central government should be limited to the minimum necessary, but they should be strictly enforced by the central government, and the provinces should not be allowed to overstep their authority. As in Article 1, Section 10 of the US Constitution, there should be strict provisions prohibiting states from doing certain things. This is one point. Furthermore, among the items specified in Article 62, such as household registration, security and public order, education and culture, hygiene and epidemic prevention, transportation, and forestry and fisheries, it seems appropriate to assign them to the provinces. Another item could be added below Article 61, stipulating the concurrent powers of the central government and the provinces. When the central government does not exercise these powers, they can be delegated to the provinces for execution in accordance with the spirit of Articles 130 and 136, but once the central government exercises these powers, the laws of the provinces become invalid. This is one point. Furthermore, "local" in Article 62 of the draft constitution should exclude the provinces, so what are the provinces supposed to do? There are no regulations, and it is necessary to supplement them.

Article 63, concerning military administration, is too simplistic and does not address the specific circumstances of our country. Military interference in politics is the greatest problem in our country, and the constitution should include concrete and effective provisions on the deployment of troops, the allocation of military expenditures, the storage of military equipment, the punishment of soldiers, the restriction of military dictatorship, and the proportions of various military branches, in order to fulfill the original intention of national constitution-making and achieve the effect of restoring order and correcting chaos. Secondly, financial issues are also closely related to the unity and peace of our country, so the division of taxation should not be based on vague clauses but on the nature of taxes, with concrete and clear regulations to avoid future disputes.

(7) The Central Political System

How to create the central political system is a significant matter that deserves special discussion. Now, I will only add some criticisms to the constitutional text.

(1) The National Government Article 69 of this section stipulates that the President and the five Yuan are responsible to the National Assembly. However, the President in Section 2 of this chapter is merely a figurehead with no real power. It is unreasonable to hold someone accountable who has no power, as it goes against the principle of balanced powers and responsibilities. Moreover, if the President does not bear any real responsibility, then where does the responsibility come from? This is another legal contradiction. As for the Yuan being responsible to the National Assembly, the National Assembly only meets once every three years and is often in recess, so this so-called responsibility is merely a formality. Article 71 states that the National Government commands the army, navy, and air force. However, the National Government is a diverse organization with no single leader. To whom does the power of command belong? The constitutional text does not specify this, which seems inappropriate.

(2) The President Article 77 only sets age as a qualification for presidential candidates. Regardless of the President's actual power, it is disrespectful and negligent to prescribe such relaxed requirements for the head of state. Article 81 states that if the President or Vice-President of the Judicial Yuan or Examination Yuan resigns due to an incident during the recess of the National Assembly, the President may appoint an acting President with the consent of the National Committee. However, there are no regulations on how to replace or whether to replace legislators or censors who resign. The National Assembly is in recess for a long time, so this should be taken into consideration.

(3) The Executive Yuan According to Article 87, the powers of the Executive Yuan are shared by the various ministries. According to Article 90, important matters are decided by meetings. Therefore, the Premier of the Executive Yuan has no real power. However, according to Article 86, the Premier of the Executive Yuan must resign if he loses a vote of confidence in the Legislative Yuan or is impeached by the Control Yuan. It is legally untenable to subject a figurehead with no real power to the double burden of responsibility. Moreover, according to Article 86 alone, if the National Committee rejects a vote of no confidence from the Legislative Yuan or an impeachment from the Control Yuan, how should the conflict between the Executive Yuan and the Legislative Yuan/Control Yuan be resolved? What responsibilities should the Legislative Yuan and Control Yuan bear in this case? There is no provision for any of this. The Executive Yuan is severely restricted and has no real power, while the Legislative Yuan and Control Yuan are unrestrained. If they abuse their power, how will it be prevented, and how will the Executive Yuan promote administrative affairs, observe national conditions, and observe the changes in the world? It is hoped that this political system will be amended.

(4) The Legislative Yuan The Legislative Yuan in this draft constitution is merely a consultative body. As stipulated in the previous chapter, there are already two major political power organs, the National Assembly and the National Committee, so the number of legislators does not need to be as high as two hundred. Article 95 states that the Legislative Yuan has the power to decide on other important international matters. The term "important" is easily subject to subjective interpretation and can easily cause disputes. Such wording should not be included in the constitution. Article 96, Paragraph 2, intertwines inquiries and no-confidence motions, making it easily exploited by ambitious individuals and causing political turmoil. Moreover, according to the previous section, the no-confidence motion should be submitted to the National Committee, but this is not clearly stated here. Furthermore, if the no-confidence motion fails to pass, it is not stipulated whether the Legislative Yuan should be dissolved and re-elected. Even from the perspective of traditional constitutional principles, this is also inappropriate.

(5) The Judicial Yuan There is ongoing debate as to whether the Department of Judicial Administration should belong to the Judicial Yuan or the Executive Yuan, with no consensus reached. This draft constitution boldly places it under the Judicial Yuan, presumably to protect judicial independence. Judicial independence is a matter of course, and we cannot disagree. However, judicial independence should also have its correct definition, referring only to the independence of the judiciary. As for judicial policy, it is closely related to the overall policy of the country and should not be allowed to follow its own course. This is why the judicial departments of various countries are subordinate to the Executive Yuan. Therefore, the appropriateness of the constitutional provisions is still to be discussed.

(6) The Examination Yuan The draft constitution does not mention the Examination Committee, presumably because such an agency does not need to be permanent, which shows a spirit of economy and seems to be an improvement over the current system. However, examinations are a major policy of the country, and the status of the members of the Examination Committee should be very respected. How they should be appointed and how they should be set up should also be specified in the constitution.

(7) The Control Yuan The powers of the Control Yuan, their scope of exercise, and their methods of exercise are not specified in detail, which may increase the difficulty of exercising them in the future. This should be elaborated on. (To be continued)

＝The whole city flies flags at half-mast and all institutions are closed＝

Yesterday was the anniversary of the martyrdom of the 72 Martyrs of Huanghuagang. All institutions, groups, and schools in the city closed for a day, flew flags at half-mast to express mourning, and held a memorial meeting at the city party headquarters in Fenglin Bridge at 9:00 AM. Strict Security 110

Yesterday, all institutions, schools, groups, party headquarters at all levels, and shops in the city flew flags at half-mast and closed for the day to show mourning. Inspectors and detectives from the Public Security Bureau patrolled the streets. Additional double posts were stationed at the border between the Chinese and foreign concessions and at key transportation routes. Security was very strict.

However, due to the non-arrival of military supplies, it had to be postponed. But the news was leaked and could not be delayed for long. Therefore, Comrade Huang Keqiang went to Guangzhou on March 29th to make arrangements, with attacks from four directions. Huang Keqiang himself attacked the Governor's Office, Yao Yuping attacked Xiaobeimen, Chen Jiongming attacked the Police Training Institute, and Hu Yisheng guarded Dananmen. At that time, Huang had already entered the Governor's Office, but the other three routes could not proceed simultaneously. Huang was defeated due to being isolated. The number of dead was probably more than seventy-two. Later, because only seventy-two bodies were found, only this number is known. Because of this uprising, there was the recovery of Wuhan that year. We believe that this commemoration is of the greatest significance, because the martyrs sacrificed for the nation. Their goal at the time was not only in Guangzhou, nor was it just to overthrow the Qing Dynasty. Because since the Qing Dynasty entered China, internal affairs have become increasingly corrupt, and the people have been increasingly oppressed. The Premier, in view of this situation, rose up in revolution. The Premier's revolutionary goal was the whole world, with China as the starting point. Therefore, today, in commemorating the martyrs, we should emulate their spirit of struggle and complete the Premier's will. The New Life Movement recently promoted by Chairman Chiang aims at self-cultivation and the vigorous implementation of propriety, justice, integrity, and a sense of shame. Because in recent years, social phenomena have destroyed our country's original morality. If this continues, the future of the country and the nation is unimaginable. Any country or nation that loses propriety, justice, integrity, and a sense of shame will never be able to survive. Propriety, justice, integrity, and a sense of shame are the four pillars of a country. If the four pillars are not upheld, the country will perish. The Premier advocated loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, trustworthiness, righteousness, and peace, and the purpose was also here. The promotion of the New Life Movement in this city has established a preparatory office, and a promotion association will be officially established soon. It is planned to start with cleanliness and order, so that everyone has vigor, and then concentrate on revitalizing the nation.) The rest is omitted.

The Financial Community's Attitude Toward Adopting

Gold Standard System 116

Believes it is Not a Thorough Solution

Dangers May Arise Once Implemented

Peng Xuepei's Original Proposal

The National Economic Council recently held a plenary meeting in Nanjing. It has been decided to hand over the proposal by Peng Xuepei, Vice Minister of the Interior, to adopt a transitional measure of the gold standard, to the Currency System Committee of the Ministry of Finance for research. After the research results are obtained, the Ministry of Finance will carefully consider its implementation. A reporter from the New News Agency learned that the financial community in this city believes that adopting the gold exchange standard has more disadvantages than advantages and is not a thorough solution. It should be known that China itself has neither sufficient reserves in peacetime nor the surplus to purchase overseas gold. If the gold standard is implemented, the dangers will be self-evident. However, Mr. Peng believes that the adoption of the gold standard is urgently needed for China's international trade and lending relationships. The original text of Mr. Peng's proposal is recorded below. China's international position in currency is becoming increasingly isolated. Its foreign trade and lending relationships are exposed to great risks. China suffers great losses every time the price of silver changes, as it did when the price of silver fell in 1929, and will do so again if the price of silver rises this time. The adoption of the gold standard has become an urgent need. However, there are two major difficulties in adopting the gold standard: one is that China would suddenly have a large amount of savings, and the other is that the Chinese people are accustomed to using silver and it is not easy to change this habit suddenly. In order to make the transition from the silver standard to the gold standard easier and more hopeful, it is proposed that

Transitional Measures 117

be as follows: (1) The government should allow the Central Bank to issue gold banknotes based on the same reserve ratio as silver banknotes. The guarantee reserve should not exceed 40%, and the cash reserve should not be less than 60%. The guarantee reserve can be used for public bonds or commercial bills, and the cash reserve can be used for cash, or for gold units as a 100% cash reserve, or deposits in gold standard countries. (2) Gold and silver banknotes will circulate on the market at the same time, without specifying a fixed ratio, and will be exchanged at market prices, like silver coins and copper coins on the market today. (3) The gold coin unit is equal to one-quarter of the gold unit currently used by customs. (4) The Central Bank should increase gold reserves as much as possible, issue gold banknotes, and strive to promote them. (5) Banks can

Central Bank 118

use gold banknotes in the same way as silver banknotes. (6) Private individuals who bring various gold ingots and goldware to the Central Bank or its designated agent to exchange for gold banknotes will be exempt from all handling fees. (7) Gold banknotes have unlimited legal tender status. (8) At a certain time, all government agencies' receipts and expenditures will be calculated in gold coins, but the use of gold banknotes and silver coins will still be allowed. (9) The Central Bank will take the opportunity to exchange silver for gold and gradually increase gold reserves whenever the price of silver rises. (10) The exchange of gold banknotes must be for 5,000 yuan or more. The Central Bank may pay with immediate or 60-day gold exchange rates. (11) Banks can accept gold ingots and goldware, convert them into gold coins, and use them as

Gold Coin Deposits 119

"The benefits of this transitional measure" (1) Gold in China is mainly used for ornaments and savings, not as currency. In recent years, gold exports have often exceeded imports. Adopting a transitional measure will add an important use for gold in China, that is, as a medium for domestic transactions. Although this cannot completely prevent the tendency of trade surpluses, it will undoubtedly make a considerable rescue. (2) Issuing gold banknotes will increase a new source of income for the country to improve the currency, without hindering the credit of banknotes in the slightest. (3) Increasing the number of chips on the market can achieve considerable

Increase in Prices 120

effect. (4) Most of the gold that the general public hoards or uses for decoration will be used in the financial sector. (5) Banks' gold reserves will gradually increase, and the country's gold reserves will also gradually increase. (6) The public will gradually get used to using gold coins. (7) Gradually exchange silver for gold. When transitioning to the gold standard, only a portion of the currency needs to be converted, which will not cause too drastic changes. (8) When the general public buys and sells small amounts of gold, they often suffer greatly from exploitation in and out. After adopting gold banknotes, this drawback can be avoided and the public's willingness to use gold can be increased. (9) The Central Bank's deposits abroad can be used as a reserve for gold banknotes. (10) Those who are related to

Foreign Trade 121

or have foresight will inevitably compete to use gold coins. Also, those who enter into various long-term contracts and fear that changes in the price of silver will affect their income will be happy to use the gold standard as a unit. (11) Chinese farmers use copper coins, which is enough to prove that there is no need to replace the more valuable metal with currency in China's domestic economy. However, this does not prevent the adoption of the gold standard, because smaller units can be used. For example, although France uses the gold standard, its unit, the franc, is only worth two dimes in our country. Today, the gold coin unit is about half a silver dollar, which is even more convenient for public use.

Kong Xiangxi Talks About

Ministry of Finance Improving the Currency System 122

Expanding the Mint to Coin Decimal Subsidiary Coins

The Gold Exchange Standard Plan is Under Study

Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi returned to Shanghai from Nanjing the night before last. He met with reporters at his residence yesterday morning. According to him, many people have advocated the adoption of the gold exchange standard in the past. After Mr. Peng Xuepei proposed it at the Economic Committee this time, it has been decided to hand it over to the Currency System Research Committee of the Ministry of Finance for research. Whether our country should adopt the gold exchange standard at present is too big a question and is currently under study. After the research results are obtained, the Ministry of Finance will carefully consider and decide whether to proceed. However, the report quoted my conversation last night as saying that although many countries in the world have adopted the gold standard, some have abandoned the gold standard and adopted the silver standard, which "is actually a mistake of abandoning the gold standard and adopting the gold and silver standard." As for reforming the currency system, the Economic Committee has passed a resolution to invest 16 million to proceed. However, this matter is of great importance and cannot be done in a short time. Because the silver coins used in various places in the interior are quite complicated, and the market prices of other subsidiary coins sometimes rise and fall, causing the general public to suffer great losses due to the exchange rate when money comes in and goes out. Therefore, in order to eliminate long-standing abuses and unify the currency system, the Ministry of Finance plans to expand the mint, coin new silver coins and decimal subsidiary coins, circulate them on the market, and at the same time, recall and destroy the old miscellaneous coins, so that the currency system will gradually be unified and will be actively implemented to achieve it as soon as possible.

Page 11

Chuanhe Qilun Company

League Pact Decided to Dissolve 130

Implementation Starts on April 1st

The Chuanhe Qilun Company League raised the water fee, causing Shanghai's Chuanbang merchants to stop handling goods and refuse transportation. This dispute has lasted for more than 50 days. Although various parties have mediated, it is difficult to reach a complete solution. The shipping companies have been meeting for days and after discussing the results, it was decided to dissolve the pact from April 1st, and to convene another meeting today to discuss the aftermath of the abolition of the alliance, and to redraft the new water fee. This matter is very important to the cargo transportation of the Chuanbang. In order to understand the truth behind this matter, the reporter personally went to each shipping company to investigate. The reasons are described below.

Minsheng Becomes the Target of Public Criticism 131

The Chuanhe shipping company initiated the alliance and increased the water fee, raising the price of cheap domestic products by more than double, and there are even unreasonable measures such as not distinguishing between grades and measuring ruler goods and weighing goods by the catty, which caused great opposition from the Sichuan merchants. Shanghai stopped shipping goods, and the various merchant groups in Chongqing had major negotiations with the Minsheng Company, causing the Minsheng Company to become the target of public criticism. The failure of the clever plan was probably unexpected.

Shipping Companies Negotiate to Remedy 132

Since the implementation of the new alliance fee on February 20, the shipping companies on the Chuanhe line have been affected by the suspension of cargo handling. Holding on like this for a long time has caused huge losses to the shipping companies. According to the round-trip of Shanghai-Chongqing direct shipping ships, it takes a full month, and the cost of large ships is about 20,000 yuan, and even shallow water ships cost about 10,000 yuan. If the alliance fee problem is not resolved for one day, it is difficult for the Sichuan ships to suffer invisible losses. On the 28th, representatives from Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, Jiejang, Sanbei, Yihua, and other shipping companies held a meeting at Jardine Matheson to discuss ways to open a new situation. It was generally believed that April is the high water period of the upper Yangtze River, and the water fee should also be reduced as usual. Each company is now bound by the alliance, which is not worth it. So they telegraphed the Minsheng General Company in Chongqing to ask whether the alliance agreement will continue or be dissolved after the expiration of this month.

Alliance Pact Decided to Dissolve 133

After the telegram was sent, the Minsheng General Company in Chongqing replied, and the wording was very smooth. The general idea was that the Minsheng Company is willing to cooperate sincerely with the other companies and continue the alliance on the extension of the Chuanhe shipping cooperation alliance after the expiration of the trial period. However, the Chongqing industries and gangs have severely criticized the Minsheng Company, making it difficult to extend. The general idea is like this. After receiving the Minsheng reply, the shipping companies decided to completely abolish the Chuanlun Alliance Cooperation Agreement signed on February 11 from April 1, and each of the seven companies will operate independently in order to eliminate difficulties and obstacles and develop a new situation. The unreasonable freight rates set during the alliance period will also be completely abolished, and each shipping company will negotiate a new freight rate suitable for each industry and gang to comply with.

Another Reasonable New Freight Rate Will Be Set 134

It was reported yesterday that the Chongqing merchant gangs have agreed on a new freight rate method and will implement it on April 1. The reporter asked the person in charge of each shipping company, and they said that this is only a one-sided water fee price drafted by the Chongqing merchant gangs, which is difficult for the shipping companies to agree to. According to the quantity and ruler freight price, each ton is only 11 yuan, and the freight price to Hankou is more than this amount. This and the 100 yuan per ton set by the alliance are both unreasonable mistakes. This news may have some effect, but let's not discuss it for now. However, after the dissolution of the alliance, the shipping companies have agreed to divide the Chuanhe freight into three periods: high water, normal water, and shallow water. The main cotton yarn water fee will be reduced to 16 yuan during shallow water, 14 yuan during normal water, and 12 yuan during high water. For those who calculate by ruler, it is planned to charge 2 yuan per ruler during normal water, 20% discount during high water, and 25% increase during shallow water. This is the fairest. Other goods will be divided into grades and levels, and no slight bias will be allowed.

Another Meeting Will Be Convened Today 135

The Chuanhe shipping company's dissolution of the alliance is only two days away from today and must be implemented. Since the new water fee price is determined to be reasonable, each shipping company has agreed to convene the seven shipping companies at Sanbei today to hold a large meeting to discuss the aftermath of the dissolution of the alliance, and the new water fee for each cargo will be re-negotiated and revised at today's meeting. Once it is determined, it will be notified to the Sichuan merchants, so that the dispute between the merchants and shipping industries on the Chuanhe River for more than 50 days, and the suspension of cargo handling by the Sichuan foreign miscellaneous goods gangs, can be resolved under today's meeting. A storm can come to an end from now on.

Appeal from the Egg Industry 136

Letter from the Chamber of Commerce to the Authorities

Requesting Reduction of Tariffs and Freight Rates

The Egg Industry Association sent a letter to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday, requesting a reduction in tax rates and freight costs, which stated: "To whom it may concern, since the successive increases in taxes both domestically and internationally, as well as the increased levels of railway freight rates, our industry has been burdened to the point of unsustainability. As a result, nearly eight or nine out of ten businesses have been forced to close. A small number of manufacturers in Fujian, unwilling to see the egg industry completely disappear, are attempting to persevere and salvage what they can. However, with the continuous sharp decline in market prices over the years, losses have been enormous, leading to utter failure and an irreparable situation. Therefore, on the 26th of this month, we convened an emergency meeting to discuss remedial measures. The consensus was that without a reduction in export taxes and railway freight rates, the egg industry has no possibility of continuing to survive. We are now detailing the reasons for the requested reductions separately as follows: According to the current customs tax rates, egg yolk powder is subject to a regular tax of 12 yuan per 100 kilograms, plus a 10% disaster relief surcharge and a 3% dock tax, totaling 13.56 yuan. The selling price is only 41 yuan. After deducting taxes, the actual revenue is 27.44 yuan. The ratio of selling price to customs tax is 50%. For wet egg yolk, the regular tax is 3.9 yuan per 100 kilograms, plus a 10% disaster relief surcharge and a 3% dock tax, totaling 4.407 yuan. The selling price is only 16.535 yuan. After deducting taxes, the actual revenue is 12.128 yuan. The ratio of selling price to customs tax is just over 36%. This error is due to the fact that the valuation when the tax regulations were revised at the time is vastly different from the current market price. Without a revaluation, manufacturers will find it extremely difficult to bear the burden. This is the reason why the export tax should be reduced. Regarding railway freight rates, egg products have always been classified as fourth-class. Since August 1, 1932, fees have been charged according to the newly revised freight classification table, with egg yolk powder and egg white reclassified as second-class, and wet egg yolk reclassified as third-class. Our association has repeatedly petitioned the Ministry of Railways to restore the old classification in order to alleviate the burden on manufacturers and maintain the precarious situation of the industry. We were granted approval for a one-year trial period, and the request was temporarily deferred. Now, the one-year trial period has long passed, and freight rates have not been reduced. In reality, whether the railway bureau's income has increased remains unknown. Continuing in this manner will only result in a lose-lose situation for both the railway and the businesses. What manufacturers find particularly painful is that second-class goods cannot be packed together with third and fourth-class goods. There are few second-class goods, so we must wait until they are fully loaded before shipping, which delays the deadline and causes the goods to spoil. The resulting losses are even greater. If we change to less-than-carload shipping, the freight costs become even higher. How can the struggling egg industry bear such heavy blows? This is the reason why railway freight rates should be reduced. Regarding the above two requests, we earnestly hope that your esteemed association will immediately send a telegram to the Ministry of Industry and also send telegrams separately to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Railways. Regardless of whether our requests can be granted, we request a prompt reply to determine our course of action. Even if the government cannot understand the difficulties of manufacturers and prevent closures, it should consider the hundreds of thousands of unemployed workers across the country. This matter concerns the survival of the entire industry. We earnestly hope for your strong assistance and separate handling of these issues."

Sudden Change in Weng Wenhao's Condition 138

Suffering from Meningitis, Onset is Quite Severe

Ding Wenjiang Has Gone to Hangzhou to Visit

According to the Central News Agency, Mr. Weng Wenhao, Director of the Geological Survey of the Academia Sinica, was injured in a car accident near Wukang on the Beijing-Hangzhou National Highway on the 16th of last month. At that time, his condition was considered to be relatively good. However, the bone fragments embedded in his brain should have been surgically removed immediately, but there were concerns about potential complications. Therefore, it was planned to perform the surgery after a period of convalescence. In addition to Dr. Goodchild of Guangji Hospital providing nearby treatment, Drs. Niu and Engel returned to Shanghai. According to a telegram received by a close friend of Mr. Weng's in this city a few days ago from Hangzhou, Mr. Weng has developed meningitis due to the abnormal weather recently, and the onset has been very severe, with talk of preparing for his final affairs. Mr. Ding Wenjiang and other friends of Mr. Weng's have now gone to Hangzhou to investigate and consult with doctors in Hangzhou for thorough treatment. However, it is reported that he is still in critical condition.
