Education News

First Meeting of the Board of Directors of the Cultural Construction Association 205

Passed the Articles of Association, Program Guidelines, and Establishment Declaration

Elected Standing Directors and Elected Chen Lifu as Chairman

The Chinese Cultural Construction Association held its first board of directors meeting at the Shanghai United Association yesterday afternoon at 4 p.m., followed by the first temporary standing director meeting. The articles of association, program guidelines, organizational regulations, and establishment declaration were passed. The details are recorded as follows:

Board of Directors Meeting 206

The directors present were Chen Lifu, (Wu Kaixian acting for) Wu Tiecheng, (Wu Xingya acting for) Wu Xingya, Pan Gongzhan, Yu Jingtang, Chen Bulei, Wu Kaixian, Shi Liangcai, (Ma Yinliang acting for) Wu Dajun, Yang Gongda, Ye Xiufeng, (Tang Huimin acting for) Hong Ludong, Zhu Yingpeng, Liu Zhuang, Cheng Zhonghang, Wang Boqi, Zhang Zhuping, Pei Fuheng, Zhang Shouyong, Shen Pengfei, Li Zhaohuan, Liu Zhanen, Ouyuan Huai, Tao Baichuan, Guo Wei, Hu Jianzhong, Weng Yuanlong, Li Denghui, Ding Mocun, Ai Yuying, (Fang Huanru acting for) Tong Xingbai, Cheng Tianfang, and 33 others. The alternate directors present were Zhu Xinong, Jiang Jianbai, Lin Zhongke, Han Juemin, Fang Huanru, Tang Huimin, Chen Bai, Wang Xinming, Li Zhiyun, Liao Yunpeng, and 11 others. The chairman was Pan Gongzhan, the recorder was Huang Jingzhai. After the chairman gave a report, the following was discussed: (1) The proposed amendments and adoption of the association's articles of association, program guidelines, organizational regulations, and establishment declaration. It was resolved to adopt them. The text will be organized by Tao Baichuan, Zhu Xinong, and Chen Bulei, designated by the chairman, and submitted to the standing director meeting for approval. (2) The determination of the number of vice-chairmen and standing directors. It was resolved that there would be two vice-chairmen and 17 standing directors, and Chen Lifu was elected as chairman, Shao Yuan Chong and Wu Tiecheng as vice-chairmen, and Zhu Jiahua, Chen Bulei, Zhang Daofan, Wu Xingya, Pan Gongzhan, Li Denghui, Ouyuan Huai, Shen Pengfei, Ye Xiufeng, Zhang Shouyong, Pei Fuheng, Li Zhaoxian, Weng Wenlong, and Liu Zhanen as standing directors. (3) Whether the association should elect honorary directors. It was resolved that honorary directors should be elected. (4) Whether an honorary chairman should be appointed. It was resolved to be decided by the standing director meeting. Then a photo was taken and the meeting adjourned. After the meeting, a temporary standing director meeting was held, attended by Wu Xingya and 12 others. The chairman was Pan Gongzhan. The establishment declaration, organizational regulations, articles of association, and program guidelines were amended and adopted. The following is recorded:

Work Program 207

The work of the China Cultural Construction Association shall be in accordance with the following program: (1) Affirm the Three Principles of the People as the supreme principle of the Chinese cultural construction movement, promote China's inherent culture on the one hand, absorb foreign culture on the other hand, actively promote the national spirit, scientific spirit, unifying spirit, and creative spirit, and passively eliminate feudal ideas, class ideas, decadent ideas, and slave ideas, in order to build a new culture suitable for modern China and seek the revival of the Chinese nation. (2) In academic research, promote the spirit of rigor, diligence, independence, and self-respect, establish the belief of creating culture, serving the people, and contributing to the country and nation, and reject the bad habits of following blindly, being superficial, and exaggerating. (3) In the literary and artistic movement, promote positive, broad, forward-looking, and vibrant national literature and art centered on national interests, and reject false, inferior, servile literature and art that promotes cruelty, proletarian literature and art, romantic, cynical, frivolous literature and art, and all literature and art that lead the nation to coldness, feudalism, and decadence. (4) In all publishing undertakings, do our best to promote the national interest as the guideline. Whether it is to introduce modern ideas, clarify the international situation, absorb foreign culture, or record domestic affairs, the goal is to not violate the national position and not harm national health. Absolutely abandon all writings and publications that destroy national self-confidence, hinder national unity, and obstruct national progress. (5) For all intellectuals, promote the atmosphere of contributing ability and sacrificing personal freedom, with creation, service, struggle, and labor as the creed, with sacrificing everything for oneself as the ultimate goal, creating a spirit of loyalty, hard work, chivalry, and righteousness, and eliminating the bad habits of seeking comfort, taking shortcuts, being decadent, passive, undisciplined, and selfish. (6) In order to change the general social atmosphere, promote the importance of propriety, justice, integrity, and a sense of shame as the center, renew the people's living habits, and strive to make diligence, simplicity, neatness, and cleanliness the basis for personal life, and to have a sense of responsibility, discipline, faith in leaders, and obedience to the group in group life. (7) In order to lay the foundation for national revival, promote national sports as much as possible and disseminate health knowledge in order to eliminate the accumulated weakness and cultivate a strong and courageous spirit, and enhance the ability of self-strengthening and self-defense. (8) In the construction of national politics, society, and economy, advocate the implementation of control centered on the Three Principles of the People, point out the fallacies of communism and capitalism, and eliminate the claims of class struggle and free competition.

Establishment Declaration 208

The rise and fall of a country, the prosperity and decline of a nation, are tied to culture. Only with the continuous replacement of the old and production of the new in culture can both the country and the nation achieve their boundless and unprecedented development. Our Chinese nation has stood for five thousand years. Tracing back to the times of Fuxi and Shennong, our ancestors had creations in every generation. The Tang, Yu, and Three Dynasties were passed down from the ancient sages, and the cultural relics and systems were brilliant and well-prepared. In terms of the long history of culture, the world rarely has its equal. It is not just the pre-Qin scholars who formed the glory of the country. The reputation of the Han and Tang Dynasties spread far to foreign lands. Even today, the national situation is deeply troubled, but this Chinese nation of 470 million people is still linked by the same cultural belt. As for the neighboring countries that have been nurtured by this culture, there are the Japanese, Siamese, Korean, and Annamese peoples. If our people do not slack in the work of replacing the old and producing the new, it will not be difficult for our country's culture to surpass all other cultures. What is a pity is that in the past 100 years, cultural evolution and elimination have been worrying. Some stick to the old ways and others blindly embrace new ways. Some stop in the middle, while others rush to a dead end. The former cling to the past and do not know the new, nearly holding onto the remnants and guarding the gaps. How can it be possible to promote and carry forward the culture? The latter know hunger but do not choose food, which is no different from drinking poison to quench thirst. Thought poisoning is even more tragic. As a result, culture has declined, the country has lost its vitality, the nation has lost its lively and enterprising spirit, and society has fallen into a corrupt and degenerate situation. Although there was a political revolution in 1911, it did not help the backwardness of culture. At this time of survival and the interruption of traditions, if we do not urgently engage in the new construction of Chinese culture, can the country and nation have any hope of revival? This is why the Chinese Cultural Construction Association was established. However, the new construction of Chinese culture should be tailored to the needs of the times. It is necessary to ensure that the construction of the new Chinese culture and the creation of a new national life complement each other. Then, the replacement of the old and production of the new in culture will be sufficient to be a tool for generating national power, and the regeneration and transformation of national life will be sufficient to be a factor in the development of culture. Only by advancing on both fronts can we pull this country and nation through the dangerous and difficult path of danger and gradually move toward the open path of unity and revival. This association believes that cultural undertakings are undertakings that benefit both the past and the future in national life. The construction of a new culture is measured only by what the new life needs. Therefore, promoting and carrying forward the inherent culture is an urgent task, and absorbing and integrating foreign culture is also necessary. Those who adhere to the old should adhere to what they should adhere to. Respecting the dregs of the previous generation, even if they are approved by the ancient sages, should be discarded like legacy. Those who innovate should innovate what they should innovate. If it is not permitted by the national conditions, then even if it is popular in the world, it must be hated like an enemy. Only in this way can those engaged in the cultural movement be able to not forget the Chinese nation at this time and in this place, and be able to cut through thorns and open up a bright opportunity for our country and nation. Moreover, in all undertakings, there must be something to take and something to give up. Taking the true depends on the courage to give up. Today, in order to complete the great cause of revitalizing the country and the nation, what is needed is the active construction of culture, and at the same time, we must devote ourselves to passive destruction. Pearls and gravel can stand for a long time, but fragrant herbs and stinking weeds must interfere with each other. If you want to accomplish the work of cultivation, you should have the power of weeding. It is sufficient to speak from a negative point of view. Eliminating the remnants of feudal consciousness, sweeping away the ideas of class struggle, saving the decadent atmosphere, and correcting the habits of slaves are all urgent tasks. Destroying the fortifications and eliminating the source requires strength. From a positive point of view, promoting the national spirit, advocating scientific knowledge, promoting the unified life of the group, and honing the great creative perseverance are all the demands of the times. This association is willing to work with the people of the country to jointly undertake them. It is hoped that the small intention will be believed by comrades and understood by the people of the country. Not only will our national culture have a bright future, but the revival of the country and the nation can also be expected in the near future. This is the declaration.

Organizational Regulations 209

Article 1. These Regulations are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 15 of Chapter 4 of the Articles of Association of this Association. Article 2. In accordance with the provisions of Article 12 of Chapter 4 of the Articles of Association of this Association, the Board of Directors shall mutually elect 11 to 17 standing directors to form the Standing Directors Meeting to perform all its duties during the adjournment of the plenary meeting of the Board of Directors. Article 3. In accordance with Article 13 of Chapter 4 of the Articles of Association of this Association, the Board of Directors shall appoint one chairman and two vice-chairmen to lead all association affairs and shall be ex officio standing directors. Article 4. In accordance with Article 14 of Chapter 4 of the Articles of Association of this Association, several honorary directors shall be appointed, who shall be appointed by the Board of Directors from those who are enthusiastic about supporting this Association. If necessary, one honorary chairman may be appointed to guide the progress of this Association. Article 5. The Board of Directors shall appoint one secretary-general, who shall concurrently serve as the order of the chairman and vice-chairmen and the Standing Directors Meeting, and handle all daily affairs, who shall be appointed by the Board of Directors from among the directors. Article 6. The Board of Directors shall establish the following groups under the secretary-general for handling association affairs: Group A, the Organization Group, shall handle registration, guidance, investigation and other matters; Group B, the Editorial and Review Group, shall handle compilation, translation, solicitation, review, publication and other matters; Group D, the Administrative Group, shall handle all accounting, general affairs, communication and other matters. Article 7. Each group in the preceding article shall have one director and one deputy director, who shall be elected by the Directors Meeting. Article 8. The persons in charge of the various business committees stipulated in Article 24 of Chapter 6 of the Articles of Association of this Association shall be elected by the Standing Directors Meeting of the Board of Directors in accordance with the provisions of Article 23 of Chapter 6 of the Articles of Association of this Association. The candidates for its members shall also be approved by the Standing Directors Meeting. Article 9. When the Standing Directors Meeting deems it necessary, it may establish various ad hoc committees to preside over or design temporary special tasks. Article 10. The plenary meeting of the Board of Directors shall be held every two months, and a temporary plenary meeting may be convened by the Standing Directors Meeting when necessary. Article 11. The Standing Directors Meeting shall be held every two weeks, and a temporary Standing Directors Meeting may be convened by the chairman and vice-chairmen when necessary. Article 12. A quorum for the plenary meeting of the Board of Directors shall be one-third or more of the total number of directors present, and a quorum for the Standing Directors Meeting shall be more than half of the total number of standing directors present. Article 13. When the Board of Directors or the Standing Directors Meeting is held, the chairman shall be the ex officio chairman. If the chairman is absent, the vice-chairman shall act as chairman. If the vice-chairman is also absent, another temporary chairman shall be elected to act as chairman. Article 14. The detailed rules for the operation of the various committees and groups under the Board of Directors shall be determined separately. Article 15. These Regulations shall be implemented after being approved by the Board of Directors, but may be amended by the Board of Directors upon the resolution of the Standing Directors Meeting or the request of ten or more directors.

▲Director of Educational Funds Resigns

▲Director of Education Reportedly Will Not Return to Kaifeng

College Admission and Career Guidance Workshop 214

▲To be Held at Wuben Girls' Middle School for Three Days Starting April 1st

▲Lecturers Include Yang Weiyu, He Qingru, Pan Yangyao, etc.

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau's Committee for Implementing College Admission and Career Guidance for Primary and Secondary Schools previously held a meeting and decided to hold a workshop at the Municipal Wuben Girls' Middle School on Huangjiaque Road for three days starting April 1st. It is reported that notices have been sent to the principals of all primary and secondary schools and the grade supervisors of the graduating classes this summer, requesting them to attend the lectures on time. Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Culture Society 215

The Shanghai branch of the Chinese Culture Society held its second preparatory meeting at 5 PM yesterday at the society's premises at 76 Huanlong Road. The attending preparatory committee members included Weng Zhilong, Shen Pengfei, Li Zhaohuan (represented by Liu Panzhu), Pei Fuheng, Chen Jinmin, Xiao Zuolin, Feng Jiangtao, Ni Wenya, Rong Qizhao, She Zuozhen, Liu Bingli, Zhang Yunfu, and Wang Lide. The meeting was chaired by Liu Bingli, with Yin Zuozhen as the recorder. First, the chairman reported on the first preparatory meeting, read the announcement from the general society, the general society's work plan, and the general society's book editing plan. Then, proposals were discussed until 7:30 PM when the meeting adjourned. The following resolutions were made: (1) The deadline for soliciting basic and youth members is set for April 10th, with quotas allocated based on the population size of different areas; (2) Pei Fuheng, Liu Bingli, and Rong Qizhao were appointed as members of the Membership Qualification Review Committee; (3) The inaugural meeting is scheduled for 2 PM on Sunday, April 15th (the location will be announced after it is finalized); (4) It was decided that the branch society will directly elect nine directors and five alternate directors at the inaugural meeting, and submit them to the general society for record; (5) Wu Tiecheng, Pan Gongzhan, Liu Bingli, Li Zhaohuan, Pei Fuheng, Weng Zhilong, and Shen Pengfei were appointed as the temporary presidium for the branch society's inaugural meeting; (6) Liu Bingli was appointed as the overall person in charge of preparing for the branch society's inaugural meeting; (7) Chen Jinmin, Liu Bingli, Xiao Zuolin, Ni Wenya, and Zhang Yunfu were appointed to draft the branch society's work plan.

Ministry of Education Forbids the Use of British Weights and Measures 216

The Ministry of Education issued a circular on the 28th to all educational institutions nationwide, instructing all levels of schools not to continue using British weights and measures and not to purchase British feet.

City Center Phase II Project

Construction of Museum and Sports Field Scheduled 217

=Sports Field Construction to Begin in June and Be Completed Next Summer=

=Museum Design Approved, Construction to Begin Within the Year=

=Financial Bureau Actively Planning Funding=

Following the Shanghai Municipal Government's relocation to the city center area, it is actively proceeding with the implementation of the Greater Shanghai Plan. It has now been decided that the Municipal Grand Sports Field and the Museum, which are part of the Phase II project, will begin construction in June of this year, one after the other. The project is budgeted at 2 million yuan, which will be raised by the Municipal Finance Bureau through the issuance of public bonds or a type of exchangeable bond. The project will begin after the proposal is submitted to the Municipal Council for discussion and approval. The construction plan for the Qiujiang Wharf has also been reviewed and completed by Director Shen of the Public Works Bureau. Our reporter has made special inquiries and recorded the details as follows:

▲Scheduled Start of Sports Field Construction: The existing First Park site in the city center area will be expanded to build a large-scale sports field. The field will cover an area of 300 acres, and its various facilities will be the most complete in the country. The entire plan has been completed. According to sources from the City Center Area Architect's Office, it has been decided that construction of the field will begin in June of this year, and bidding and other work will begin soon. Construction must be completed before the summer of next year so that the National Games in 1935 and the Far Eastern Games in 1936 can be held at the field, and therefore, no further delays can be tolerated.

▲Museum Design Approved: The construction of the Municipal Museum, which was decided by the Municipal Government as part of the Phase II plan for the city center area, is also scheduled to be implemented within this year. The design for the museum was previously drafted, but due to some changes, it was redesigned by architect Dong Dayou to meet practical needs. The design for the museum has now been completed and has been discussed and approved by the Municipal Museum and Library Preparatory Committee at a meeting. After some minor revisions in the coming days, it will be completely finalized. The exterior will still be in the palace style with Chinese artistic elements, and it will be quite magnificent and beautiful. The museum will begin construction within this year, following the sports field.

▲Finance Bureau to Raise Funds: The funds for the realization of the above-mentioned construction projects are being actively planned by Cai Zengji, Director of the Municipal Finance Bureau. However, given the city's extremely difficult financial situation, the Municipal Government itself will find it difficult to bear the full burden for the time being. After discussions among the directors of the Municipal Government's various bureaus, it was decided that the Municipal Finance Bureau should plan to borrow from the banking sector or issue bonds. The methods under consideration include: (1) the Municipal Government borrowing from the financial sector, with the Municipal Treasury allocating funds for repayment in installments; (2) issuing municipal public bonds; (3) issuing a type of exchangeable bond, allowing citizens to directly purchase the bonds, which can then be used to pay municipal taxes and duties in full. It is said that the amount is 3 million yuan, which will be used for the sports field and museum. The planning for the museum's furnishings and equipment is to be postponed. After deliberation and decision on the above methods, they will be submitted to the Municipal Council for formal implementation and approval.

Free Talk

On Editors 218

— Ah Dai

Interacting with words is called "discussion," directly speaking is called "saying." Since no one is talking about it, I will speak directly. In other words, this "saying" is the "I gave him a talking to" kind of saying, the saying of right and wrong, the saying of gossip. It contains the meaning of criticizing, inciting, and persuading. Editors encompass all editors of newspapers, magazines, regular publications, and irregular publications in the world. What is there to say about editors? I will now say it below...

The literary world is currently abuzz with the "He Xu authorship issue." The "Beijing School" considers it a disgrace to the "Shanghai School," taking the manuscript of an unestablished writer and attaching an established name to submit it to a publication, as if opening a factory or running an exchange. But one is willing to give away, and the other is willing to receive; one simply doesn't want to be named, doesn't want royalties, and the other simply wants to take the credit, wants to take other people's manuscripts, and also take responsibility for the writing. We won't delve into their rights and wrongs. What I want to say here is... a group of editors cannot avoid taking some responsibility for this matter.

Manuscripts by writers without fame do not receive the favor of editors. This is a universal lament. But editors are not dormitory supervisors, and the court has not entrusted them with evaluating and selecting talents. Why so harshly dismiss all new writers? It is said that a certain magazine company once moved (this was a long time ago), and workers carried out six or seven boxes, all filled with unsolicited manuscripts, still sealed in their original envelopes, with the words "Unread" written on them! This is probably called "Even with seven boxes, it doesn't make a newspaper."

Even for editor-gentlemen who are humble and willing to accept good advice, they establish their own opinions and revise manuscripts into a complete mess. For example, when giving someone a flower, it is protected with green leaves. The editor likes this one flower and removes all the branches and leaves because he is "limited by space." Or they subtly delete one or two words in crucial places, like a painting of a beautiful woman that has already undergone the artist's painstaking efforts, but they take colored paint and smear it on the expressive eyes, a slight change that alters the entire view. Even when they easily let it pass, they are not satisfied and must add an editor's note or repeatedly praise it, thus wronging the author, misinterpreting the original meaning, and causing discouragement. Or they split up a work that clearly cannot be divided and publish it in parts; or they deliberately place the manuscript in an inappropriate position...

Therefore, I say that the current mess of authorship involving He and Xu originates from the shame of modern editors. Manuscripts by unknown writers have no way of appearing. Countless talented works are silently submerged! Everyone is following the old ways, agreeing with each other, without feeling the mission of their work in an era of culture!

Changsha Sesame Twist 219

— Lan Ru

It was a quiet, late night. I was awakened by the noisy sound of a huqin, and the lamplight coming in from the street lamp was so dim and desolate that it was frightening. Looking out from the window, the sky was pitch black, without even a tiny star. The two pots of orchids placed on the windowsill looked like a pair of disheveled wild ghosts. I stared, rubbing my eyes with extra effort. The disheveled hair seemed to be blown by a storm, rushing towards me. I was a little scared and quickly pulled my head back under the covers. Who knew that the disheveled hair would turn into two huge black shadows, walking towards me step by step? I tightly covered my head with the blanket, holding a heart that was beating wildly.

The black shadows were actually pressing down on my body, and I felt extremely difficult to breathe.

"Don't scare yourself. Those are two pots of orchids. Where are there any ghosts?"

Clearly, something in my mind seemed to be telling me not to have such unconscious fantasies.

But I broke out in a cold sweat, and my clothes were soaked. I still dared not stick my head out. "Changsha sesame twist, white sugar rice flower." [Note 1]

I vaguely heard this cry that I was used to hearing every night, and I seemed to gain courage. I stuck my head out, and the black shadows of the orchids seemed even more terrifying. They looked like a hideous face, almost like a yaksha. I quickly turned my head away and thought carefully.

At this moment, I was completely awake!

Orchid was originally the name of a friend, and it contained a particularly profound meaning. Unfortunately, he had just died a month ago. When I bought the orchids, I never dreamed that he would die so quickly, so tragically.

Could it be that his soul had come tonight?

I became a little superstitious. Yes, a person will always unconsciously fall into the circle of superstition at some point.

The cry of "Changsha sesame twist, white sugar rice flower" was getting closer and closer. The bell of the wonton seller was also ringing. Strangely, they seemed to be standing still under my window, calling and ringing.

I began to feel annoyed. I felt that they shouldn't be disturbing people's sleep. If I hadn't been awakened by the huqin player, wouldn't I be in sweet dreams right now? And I wouldn't have discovered the terrible black shadows on the windowsill.

Thinking of this, I became even more annoyed.

"Yali," [Note 2] "did you make a lot of money tonight?"

They began to talk, and I knew that this was the wonton seller asking the child selling sesame twists.

"Not even two hundred cash. How can I go home like this?"

"There's no business. I've never gone out as soon as it gets dark, and I've only made a little over a dime by now. It's too cold these past two days, and people are sleeping early, so there's no business."

"What cold or not cold, people with money have stoves burning at home, so they're warm and comfortable even if it snows. They play cards until dawn and have concubines serving them cigarettes, and servants and maids pouring tea next to them. Yali, why don't you go to the entrance of the big mansions?"

"Hmph! Big mansions? They won't eat your bowl of wontons. They have sea cucumbers and bird's nest at home."

"Yali, stop complaining here and hurry up! It's almost dawn!"

"Changsha sesame twist, white sugar rice flower..." This sound faded far away in the air like sad music, and the sound of the bell also disappeared with it.

[Note 1] Both are types of candy, specialties of Changsha.

[Note 2] Yali is a term for child.

Answer Question 220

— Zang Kejia

I just came from the countryside. You don't need me to say a word. You only need to look at my face or smell my clothes. I truly know everything there, know everything, like a child knows their mother. He knows clearly how long is the hair on her body. What do you want to ask? Are you asking about the hazy willows on the long embankment in the misty rain of the Qingming Festival? Or the peach blossoms reflecting on the cheeks of girls in the setting sun and spring breeze? Ask about the coolness seeping out of the mountain stream in the hot summer, bats flying around the ancient temple in the hazy dusk? What else do you want to ask? Ask about the beauty of the autumn mountains, the rolling clouds in the autumn wind, the desolate coolness of the setting sun on the boundless wilderness? I know you want to ask about the eight crowing sounds of the rooster in the winter night, an old woman rocking a spinning wheel, watching a dim little lamp. You want to ask this, I am all familiar with this, but what I want to tell you are some other things. Don't be alarmed after listening, and there's no need to sigh. That makes you seem so ignorant. I'm telling you, the villagers in the countryside are now tightening their belts and enduring the depths of spring. They haven't let down their guard. In the wind and cold, they bury their bodies on the slopes. They sow seeds in the spring, planting them in the earth, but they no longer sow hope as they used to. You can tell a dispirited heart just by the sound of urging the cattle! They work, no longer singing joyful songs, and even the smoke from their work-relieving cigarettes doesn't bring out ease. This can't be blamed on them. A body turns with the sun and moon, and in the end, three intestines are empty, one and a half empty! The stories in the mouth of an eighty-year-old woman are no longer ancient heroes, but themselves. They say they saw the Taiping Rebellion with their own eyes, but they've never seen a year like this! Relying on the five grains can't be exchanged for money, there's either war or floods. As soon as the sun sets, panic comes. They rest their heads on pillows and hear it until dawn. The endless varieties of taxes are like a blood basin, licking dry the joy of the countryside and sucking up the flesh and blood of the poor! I'm telling you, the countryside today is a bomb, inside which is brewing the fire of explosion. × × ×

The General's Sorrow 221

— Le Bin

丨丨One of Ancient Anecdotes丨丨

"As long as you are willing to be my wife, not only will I pardon your crime, but I can give you whatever you want."

The general was captivated by the woman's beauty. After dismissing all the attendants, he gently loosened her bonds, while saying in a low and earnest voice.

The woman tilted her disheveled head and laughed loudly.

"Lower your voice. Please lower your voice!"

The general panicked and looked anxiously outside the curtain... Red bonfires dotted the peaks far and near... The soldiers' lewd songs rang out in the forest on the slope.

The woman suppressed her laughter and said...

"Then, are you willing to lead your troops for me and be my follower?"

"I am willing, I am willing... Isn't it the same whether you lead them or I lead them?"

The general shouted with joy; the shadow of his excited arm danced on the curtain. "No, if I lead your troops, I won't be as... as you!"

The woman glanced at the brightly burning silver candles on the table and refuted casually.

The general understood what she meant. He stopped loosening the ropes and asked with a look of pity...

"Why don't you ever change your mind and always oppose them?"

The woman became serious and said frankly... "Because as long as they exist, others simply cannot survive!"

The general scratched his bald head with difficulty, remained silent for a while, and then pleaded softly again...

"Can't you ask for something else?"

The woman shook her head and smiled.

"Then, when the sun rises tomorrow, you will say goodbye to this beautiful world!"

The general sighed, with a regretful expression.

"That's very good!"

The woman laughed again, her eyes shining with bright brilliance.

The general's face turned slightly pale, and his eyes were filled with disappointment and sorrow. He walked in front of the woman, quietly looked at her, and said in a very sympathetic tone...

"Can't I help you at all in the end?"

"You can help a little!"

"Which point?"

"That is, please kill me before dawn!"

"Why!"

"Because I grew up in darkness and must also perish in darkness!"

Tentative Translation of the Book of Songs 222

— Yu Shi Xia

Ge Lu (Hemp Sandals)

One

Thin, thin hemp sandals, how can they tread on frost? Tender, slender daughter's hands, how can they sew clothes? Sew the waistband and collar well, the adults will wear them without fear of the cold!

Two

The adults walk comfortably, politely yielding to the left, with ivory hairpins adorning their hair. It's just that they are too greedy, so they are scolded enough by others!

On Translation · Om 223

The matter of translation has been around for a long time! Let's briefly copy the preface to the Collection of Translated Meanings compiled by Master Fayun of Purun Temple in the Shaoxing era, to "speak up" for modern translation experts...

"Those who translate are said to turn the words of Brahma into the words of the Han land. Although the sounds are different, the meanings are largely the same. The Song Monk Biography says... It is like turning brocade embroidery, the front and back are both displayed, but the left and right are different. Translation is said to be exchange, meaning to exchange what one has for what one lacks. Therefore, the scriptures of this land are used to reveal the laws of that land. The Rites of Zhou governs the languages of the four directions, each with its own official. The east is called Ji, the south is called Xiang, the west is called Didi, and all directions are called Yi. Today, the term Yi is commonly used for Western languages, because the Han dynasty was often concerned with the north, and the translation officials also handled Western languages. When Kasyapa Matanga first arrived, he translated the Forty-Two Chapters, and thus it was called translation." Et cetera.

According to "us with the habit of textual research," this origin is actually very early. There are also translation officials in modern times, "speaking as an official," which is quite different from translation, so we don't need to worry about that. Modern translators, when translating Western books, should pay attention to several things, not just "buying a good dictionary." We respectfully present the matters as follows...

1. Deeply understand the Chinese language. Translate it like Chinese, not Japanese or Chinese spoken by foreigners, but Chinese spoken by Chinese people. However, there are several taboos:

a. Avoid flaunting erudition. Don't be verbose and don't deviate from the "main line."

b. Avoid using classical language. Zhang Guan should be Zhang Dai, not Li Dai.

c. Avoid using ancient characters. Writing ancient characters or extracting obscure characters from Han rhapsodies and adding them to the translation in order to seek its high splendor often leads to the point of "not being understood."

d. Avoid pandering. Translating Western poems into regulated verse or the Sao style has the suspicion of pandering, and the result is often that it cannot pander. And it takes too much effort. (To be continued)

"Spring sleep unaware of dawn..."

~Last Letter~ (8) 224

— Lin Huiyin

"If I had money," Zhuo Yun finally broke the silence, "I could lend you some privately. But I don't. And I originally thought I could get an advance on a month's salary, but now that's fallen through, so I've become a problem myself. I'm really sorry, please think of a solution elsewhere. Do you have any place you can think of to get help?"

At this point, Ina finally raised her eyes again and began to speak...

"I haven't thought about what to do, and even if I wanted to, it's too late now, so your kindness will easily be wasted. Even regarding you, I initially didn't think of troubling you, and if I had thought of it and known it, this trouble wouldn't have happened. Now, please believe me, now that I know, I won't bother you again."

After saying that, she stood up, ready to leave.

"I have another idea," he said, as if inspired, "but it might not work; sell your novel to some bookstore. Do you know any? Or, I could go ask for you. Whether it succeeds or not, I'll call you."

Although she knew it was hopeless, Ina still hoped that Zhuo Yun could make a phone call to her that contained even a hint of hope. But there was no phone call, no phone call from Zhuo Yun, even the most hopeless one.

"Didn't he say himself that whether it succeeded or not, he would always make a phone call?" she thought miserably. "Alas, he said it himself! What's the use of him saying it himself? Hasn't he already said a lot? Promising again and again, and then again and again not doing what he promised?

The so-called "gate" was already upon her, and the sun of the thirtieth day was already shining on the earth. Ina heard that "gate," saw that "gate," smelled that "gate," and even touched that "gate"—gloomy, sharp, and cold. But at the same time, she also felt joyfully that it was only like that that it felt like celebrating the New Year, that tense, that exciting, something that could never be had when celebrating the Gregorian New Year. If she could get a sum of money on the last day of that year to pay off all her debts, how wonderful that would be! Therefore, she was still preoccupied with that hopeless hope.

"I'll go see Xi Zhuo Yun one more time before deciding," she finally decided. And, even if she didn't go to see Xi Zhuo Yun, she still had to go out, because that way, not only could she avoid her mother's nagging, urging, and reproachful affection, but she could also escape the various expressions on the faces of the approaching debt collectors.

She was led into the guest room, and after a minute or two, the person who came in was not the Xi Zhuo Yun she wanted to see, but his wife.

"Mr. Xi has gone out, Miss Chen. Is there anything you need?" Mrs. Xi asked.

Gone out? For some reason, she didn't quite believe it. She thought he was upstairs.

"There is something," Ina reluctantly said, not wanting to lie, "but I need to talk to him in person; now that he's not here, it's nothing."

Foreign Banks Closing for Western Holiday 229

Foreign banks will be closed for three days starting today (the 30th) due to the Western Qingming Festival, as per custom, and will resume normal operations on April 3rd. Western firms and Western stores will be closed, but Chinese banks on the Bund, such as the Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and Central Bank, will remain open this year, despite also being closed for exchange.

Securities March Bonds

Delivery Volume Sees Another Increase 230

=33,655,000 Yuan=

=Silver and Banking Sectors Still Account for Most Receipts=

Yesterday was the delivery period for various bonds at the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange. Market trading was suspended for one day. The total delivery volume was 33,655,000 yuan, of which 23,015,000 yuan was cleared, representing inter-broker deliveries, while the total volume received and cleared at the exchange was 10,640,000 yuan. Off-exchange deliveries were comparatively higher, estimated at around 30 million. The total amount was quite impressive. The delivery volume has gradually increased in recent years, indicating that investment power has gradually developed. However, calculated against the total amount of government bonds, the delivery volume is relatively small, suggesting a shortage of goods and the strong creditworthiness of bonds is evident. Upon investigation, the silver and banking sectors still accounted for most receipts. On the delivery side, in addition to the Ministry of Finance's goods, a portion was also delivered by retail investors. With a stable environment and abundant funds, investment has gradually increased. Tighter lending by the silver and banking sectors has further left short positions with no way out. Market prices have gradually risen, breaking the highest record of 1933 and gradually reaching new highs. Tracing back to the March futures, which started trading on January 30th, after approximately 40 trading days, excluding over ten days of closures for the New Year and various holidays, the market price trended as follows: within the first ten days of trading, there were limited and minimal fluctuations. From February 5th and 6th, as the Lunar New Year approached, new highs were discovered. From the red opening on February 19th, the rising momentum gradually intensified, soaring gradually. The two weeks after the February delivery were the most sluggish, with extremely thin trading and constant hovering. From March 16th, the silver and banking sectors gradually increased absorption, and market prices regained flexibility, mostly rising every day, with the recent one or two weeks seeing an especially strong surge and new highs emerging one after another. The highest price for troop reduction bonds was 74 yuan and 1 jiao, and the highest price for salt tax bonds was 55 yuan and 8 jiao and 5 fen. Compared to the lowest price on February 1st, troop reduction bonds were 7 yuan and 1 jiao higher, and salt tax bonds were 5 yuan and 6 jiao and 5 fen higher. Even compared to the initial market price, there was a difference of 6-7 yuan, indicating that market prices were almost always rising. During the process, although there were unfavorable news such as the Sun Jun rebellion, the rampant activities of the Communists, the deteriorating relations between Japan and Russia, rumors about the Premier, and the United States raising silver prices, all of them failed to diminish the strong sentiment of the long positions. As the market price had reached a high level, speculators had no opportunities to take advantage of, and instead manipulated the 96 bonds. In recent days, 96 bonds surged to 12 yuan and 8 jiao, matching the highest price of last year, but were merely speculative air and not sustainable, thus soon falling sharply by two yuan and several jiao. From this, it can be seen that speculation and investment have vastly different strengths and cannot be compared. However, with market prices currently high, the future should not see much further upward momentum. Given the strong selling pressure from major players, prices may hover and decline. Grains

Longs Exit This Month's Flour 239

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning, the market for all months showed a flat and weak trend. Chicago wheat prices fluctuated by 8 to 10 cents, and Canadian wheat was up about 4 cents. However, after the opening prices were announced, market sentiment remained weak. Although scattered transactions were seen with active retail sales, large-scale shipments were quiet. It was heard that Tianjin spot sales accounted for half, while Shanghai flour only reached over 10,000 [units], which is rare. This is the reason for the poor market sentiment. By the afternoon opening, market prices for all months were also weak. Because the delivery month is approaching, many outside long positions have exited, leading to another decline of one dime. The distant months also showed fatigue. Given the current situation, if retail sales are not smooth, although a large drop is unlikely, a rise will also be difficult. As a result, this month's price fell by 1.5 cents, April fell by 1.25 cents, May fell by 1.5 cents, June fell by 1.75 cents, July fell by 1 cent, and August fell by 0.75 cents.

Dense Sell Orders in Wheat Futures Market 240

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat futures market in the morning and afternoon, the market for all months showed a consistent weak trend. This month has already passed, and there were no transactions in April or May. However, sentiment for distant new wheat has softened. Although the cold and rainy spring in various places inevitably affects the wheat seedlings, it is not a significant concern in terms of the season. Moreover, given the low demand in the new wheat season after the government wheat is completely sold out, and the sluggish flour sales, sell orders surged in both the morning and afternoon sessions, and prices fell sharply. As a result, June fell by 6 cents, July fell by 4 cents, and August fell by 5 cents. Due to mutual rejection between factories and customers, there were no spot wheat transactions.

North and South Rice Markets Decline One After Another 241

▲Shanghai South Yesterday, more than forty [rice] dealers arrived (more than 6,000 piculs). Although the weather cleared, sales in various markets were weaker than expected. Due to continuous spring rains, dealers had accumulated a lot of stock, and their intentions to buy were somewhat dampened. Sellers with larger quantities of goods were eager to sell quickly, so the market appeared active, but in reality, it had turned weak. Also, as the end of the month approached, urban and rural shops temporarily suspended purchases. Prices for Changbang, Sutong, Nangang and other japonica rice were difficult to stabilize. Higher-priced rice weakened by about 5 cents, while mid-range rice fell by nearly a dime. Duyang and Jian rice were also affected, falling by about a dime. High-quality Yin rice was able to hold its ground, while mid-quality and lower-quality rice declined. Sales of late-season rice were weak, and contracted sales continued to fluctuate. Only dealers from Beiyang, Tianjin, and Weihaiwei took deliveries, providing support to the market. As a result, the decline was uneven, ranging from 3-5 cents, 6-7 cents, to nearly a dime.

▲Shanghai North Yesterday, goods from various river dealers arrived. Inland waterways were open, and about ten dealers arrived, but sales remained sluggish. High-quality white japonica rice was stable, while mid-quality and lower-quality rice was slightly lower by a few cents. Yangdu and Jian Baiyuan rice were down slightly by 3-5 cents, and thin rice was down by nearly a dime. Merchants' Jian early rice and Yin Yuan rice were stable.

Accumulated Foreign Rice Being Sold 242

▲Small Package of 85,000 Bags...6.50 Yuan

▲Merchants from Zhejiang and Fujian Continue to Handle...Market Turning Stable

Yesterday, merchants from Wenzhou, Zhejiang province, continued to handle shipments. Merchants from Fuzhou, Fujian province, had not handled shipments for many days, but resumed handling shipments yesterday due to the favorable market prices. As a result, the market atmosphere became more active, and sentiment was hopeful. Although there were continued arrivals, the market is gradually becoming more active, so the market should stabilize temporarily. Yesterday, Fuzhou handled 400 bags of Hunan machine-milled red rice at a price of 6.90 yuan, and 122 bags of rough red rice at a price of 5.90 yuan. This price is about one dime lower than the prices quoted earlier. If the price is favorable, it may stimulate merchant activity. Wenzhou handled 1,200 bags of Nanjing Chenxian and factory Xian rice, and 288 bags of Chuzhou machine-milled Xian rice. The price was similar to the previous market, and the situation was slightly better.

Foreign rice has been quiet for a long time, and there have been no large transactions in recent months. Most of the scattered transactions on the market are goods being recovered from the local market, affected by merchant Xian rice, and prices have been unable to improve for a long time. Merchants also lack sales channels, so the inventory on the market is close to 200,000 [bags]. Yesterday, Dachen and Xinfeng rice firms negotiated with Anli Foreign Firm to sell 85,000 bags of small package rice. Because it was a bulk transaction, the price was only 6.50 yuan, which is cheaper than the market price. It is said that some of this batch of foreign rice has already been allocated by dealers.

Soybean Market Weak 243

Yesterday, the source of soybeans was still continuous, and factories were still the biggest buyers. Other channels such as local exports had some interest, but it was difficult to expect large-scale purchases, so sentiment was weak and prices fell by 1-2 cents. One truckload of Huaiyuan soybeans and one truckload of Feihe soybeans were purchased by local merchants. In addition, 300 bags of Guide soybeans and 300 bags of Feihe soybeans were for export.

Silk Market, Foreign Firms' Silk Sales in Desperate Situation 244

▲New York Raw Silk Market Active but No Sales New York silk mills, in view of the global economic downturn, the sales of silk fabrics are declining, and they are reducing production and shutting down machines to clear accumulated inventory. The consumption of raw silk has decreased significantly. Furthermore, Japanese silk is being dumped at excessively low prices, so no one is interested in Chinese silk. According to news from the American silk merchant Qianli Foreign Firm in Shanghai, in the second half of this month, the New York raw silk market for Chinese silk is almost active but without sales. Only stockpilers sold 8,000 pounds of Grade B white filature silk at an average of 81.2 points, and the selling price was only about US$1.40 per pound, equivalent to just over 480 yuan per bale converted to Chinese currency.

▲Old Cocoons from Hangzhou Actively Transported to Shanghai The spring silkworm season in Hangzhou and Shaoxing is starting, and new cocoons are quickly entering the market. Merchants with leftover old cocoons are actively transporting them to Shanghai. Yesterday, 108 loads of double cocoons were transported to Shanghai from stations such as Gengshanmen and Changan to seek sales.

▲Shanghai Silk Sales Increasingly Sluggish Overseas raw silk prices are becoming increasingly weak, the demand from various silk mills is increasingly rare, and Japanese silk is being dumped at excessively low prices, with supply exceeding demand. No one is paying attention to Chinese silk. European and American firms in Shanghai are all taking a wait-and-see approach. Mainland silk factories are buying as needed, sales are sparse, and the selling price is extremely low. Silk merchants are suffering significant losses and cannot afford to sell. The market atmosphere is becoming increasingly sluggish, and the future of silk sales is in a desperate situation.

Sharp Increase in Tunxi Tea Firms 245

The tea industry in Tunxi has always been prosperous. Since the opening of the Hangzhou [to Tunxi] highway, tea merchants have become even more excited. The British firm Baochang Foreign Firm, which handles tea in Shanghai, has established a large-scale tea factory in that city. More than twenty other newly established firms have been set up, bringing the total to more than seventy, and the situation is quite active.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

More Liberal Arts than Sciences 267

— Chen

According to reports, the Ministry of Education's recent statistics on national students studying abroad in the 21st year show a total of 576 people, with 213 studying sciences and 342 studying liberal arts, including 179 specializing in law and political science. (21 people are not specified.) Upon careful examination of this statistical table, those studying liberal arts account for more than three-fifths of the total, while those specializing in law and political science account for about one-third of the total.

At a time when the call for "reviving the nation and building the country" is rampant, there should be a great reliance on specialized and capable technical personnel. It seems that the number of Chinese students studying science and engineering should be on a sharp and rapid rise. However, according to this disclosure, things are upside down, which makes people feel deeply doubtful about this "revival and construction." Originally, China's dispatch of students to study abroad has lacked planning, which is truly a loss of the intention to "reserve talents for the country." At the same time, these students, praised as "foreign scholars" and boasting that they will contribute to the country and the nation, mostly do not belong to the young masters and sons of high-ranking officials, but are extravagant and luxurious children. Their travels to Europe, the East, and the New World are mostly for enjoyment, and they never seek trouble by burying themselves in studies. Choosing liberal arts is easier and more enjoyable for them, which is not surprising. However, in light of the current situation in China, this is not just a simple matter, but symbolizes the following two meanings:

First, the dark clouds of the global economic recession have enveloped the entire land of China. In the areas affected, rural bankruptcy, commercial depression, and industrial closures are inevitable. Coupled with years of war and endless internal strife, this vast and resource-rich country is left gasping for breath. Adding to this the unprecedented natural disaster of "three years without rain," all the beautiful plans for revival and construction have become "desirable but unattainable." Therefore, many scientific talents who "return home after completing their studies" feel lost and have no place to use their skills. Learning from the past, many people who cannot find a way out "in the vertical lines of triangles" change their course and turn to study the "great way of governing the world" in law and political science. The fact that there are more students studying liberal arts than sciences is a reflection of this social turmoil.

Second, who doesn't want wealth and luxury? In the past, the imperial examinations allowed many people, especially scholars, to enter the officialdom through beautiful essays. But now times have changed, and it is said that it is difficult to govern without understanding even a little bit of politics, legal principles, or interpretive jargon. Driven by this desire, many people indeed see studying law and political science as a shortcut to joining the ranks of officials in the central ministries. The particularly large number of students studying law and political science is also likely induced by this kind of opportunistic mentality.

In the past, during the slogan of "education is sacred," some scientific talents who studied abroad could follow the example of "circular education" and reluctantly take up teaching positions in schools when they could not "apply" what they had "learned." But now, not only is this considered a bland life, but also because it is no longer sacred, it is not easy to seek a teaching position, which is also one of the reasons contributing to more liberal arts than sciences. My wooden clogs friends often scold us for being a non-modernized country with disunified politics, but now we have one-third of the students studying abroad in various countries specializing in law and political science. How do we know that politics will not get on track and the whole country will be unified in the future? Why not respond in this way?

One of the Diary of a Soldier 268

— Jack

The sun just disappeared! Only a few almond-yellow clouds were floating in the sky. The train stopped at the station for the first time.

Jumping out of the freight car, two groups of people occupied the platform. In the gray crowd, only a few yellowish-brown tarpaulin hats could be seen. I wanted to know the name of the station; however, before I could do so, we gathered and followed the team out of the station.

It's getting late! We only had steamed buns once on the train, and we haven't had dinner yet. I don't know how much further we have to walk, and I don't know where we'll camp. It wasn't until after walking for four or five hours that we reached a village. Although there was some moonlight on the road, I kept stubbing my toes on the uneven hillsides.

We found a house of local people to stay in. Today is considered a good thing for being the vanguard, as we found a house first. Otherwise, if we arrive late, we might have to camp outdoors.

The cooks quickly cooked the meal for us to eat. The commander ordered, "No roll call tonight!" Everyone was very happy and wanted to rest early. The squad leaders were taking care of the sleeping arrangements! Some were already snoring like cows; I was also about to enter dreamland.

In an instant, a flash of light flashed across my face. Someone was talking to the guard at the door. Then, he walked in, shone a flashlight into the company commander's room. In a small voice, he was looking for the clerk sergeant. Tonight at two o'clock, a general attack. Our XX regiment is attacking San Chen Zhuang. I felt in my heart that I couldn't sleep anymore! At the same time, the company commander had already called the messengers! Just as I was thinking about getting up, the officer of the day blew the whistle, and the duty squad leader also blew the whistle. Then, there was a sound of rolling gray blankets, coughing, and bayonets falling to the ground... instantly breaking through the silent air.

It just so happened that three coolies ran away last night. All day today, the ordnance bullets in the company headquarters were carried in shifts by the first and second platoons. Now, we have to rely on the third and fourth platoons.

The company commander issued a temporary order: The third and fourth platoons are to find eight coolies. The squad leader told Liu Jinbiao and me to find four, "If you can't find them, you two will have to carry them!"

I'm most afraid of these things. It's easy for me to shoot two people, but it's really hard to find a few living people to suffer!

However, what can I do? If I don't get them, I'll have to carry them myself; but I can only carry so much alone. As I walked, that's what I was thinking.

Walking past a few houses, we only encountered some old women. Those with money and people had certainly escaped long ago. "I know; we don't need to go into houses that don't have a gate or houses that have no one."

That's what I told Liu Jinbiao. "Good! There's a gate here!" He kicked it twice and then smashed it open with the butt of his gun... I followed him inside.

Facing the gate was a hall without a door. He looked inside and walked in; I stood and looked around. That's good; there was a sound of a man asking questions inside. I continued to go in; an old man of about fifty, wearing his clothes, opened the door; two boys of seventeen or eighteen years old came out of the room next door. Wang Jinbiao spoke to him politely in Henan dialect; they didn't dare to object, nor did they say they wouldn't go. They stood there uncertainly, trying to make up their minds.

After speaking for a long time, they were still noncommittal. He got angry and gave them two gun butts. I also kicked the old man twice...

"We're here to fight for you; you're not even willing to carry things for us?" I said.

They obeyed very obediently; but I felt very remorseful in my heart. I remembered the inhuman and barbaric actions of the soldiers in our hometown during the warlord era. At that time, even though we were children, we felt so indignant and cursed them! Now, because of the pressure of the environment, this kind of unreasonable and barbaric behavior has openly been realized by myself! The reason is caused by the environment.

— Su

Treaties are only a chapter in history, not the conclusion of history.

I hope to give everyone a chance to experience that work is not a pain, but a joy of life.

I would rather prevent in advance than use oppression afterwards.

× × ×

I do not reject any advice, even from the enemy, as long as it is truly sincere.

× × ×

Only leaders who are selfless, not cowardly, not biased, and full of loyalty are loved.

× × ×

Heaven 270

— Yi Lu

丨Remember Huaibei丨

I have left Huaibei, and hastily returned to the South, without realizing that it has become a memory of more than half a year ago. When I embarked on my return journey to the South, I originally thought that we would meet again after only ten days or so of separation. Who could have imagined that this would seem to be an indefinite farewell? The traces I left in Huaibei are like fallen flowers drifting on the flowing water, traceless and no longer remembered by people; while the impressions that Huaibei gave me still appear in my mind from time to time, and have never been blurred. Huaibei is indeed lovely, making me

Page 18

reluctant to leave. In a heaven without the embellishments of the times丨What use is it to embellish heaven?丨, what is manifested everywhere is quiet harmony, the most supreme! The people there, the customs there, even every hill and every stream, every blade of grass and every tree, I regard them with utmost reverence, viewing them as sacred, and I cannot help but feel that everything is specially designed for heaven, or rather, I should say, unique to heaven!

The impression Huaibei gave me is really too deep! But... this is definitely not a bad thing. Who wouldn't want to have a deep impression of what he loves? And who wouldn't want to admire in his dreams the lover he longs to see but cannot see? 丨This is all very good, so why should I worry so much about my stubborn views? The only thing I feel is happiness, that in every moment when I recall Huaibei, all the things surrounding me gradually disappear, until it seems as if there is nothing left, only me alone.

I should always remember clearly that in the spring of the year before last, when I first entered a town in Huaibei, it was precisely when she (Huaibei) was being ravaged by bandits. At that time, the residents there were fleeing in droves, supporting the old and carrying the young, while I was carrying my luggage, embarking on my journey to meet her for the first time.

I have already said that what I first arrived at was a town in Huaibei, a small town. 丨Although, this small town later introduced me to everything in Huaibei丨At that time, everything in this town seemed very peaceful (later I learned that it was indeed peaceful, and had always been peaceful), after the footsteps of the bandits had passed. How fortunate am I? My body and mind are entrusted to a heaven that is unparalleled in its peace! But how am I to describe this heaven? I am incapable; even if I try my best, I will inevitably fall into the mundane. Then, shall I let it forever appear in my mind? That is even more impossible, as it would make me feel uneasy. Alas! Too deep an impression instead makes me hesitate and not know what to do! 丨Stop hesitating! Write down those scattered fragments first, anyway, they are all given to me by heaven.

Among the earliest things in this small town to develop a close relationship with me was the earthen wall丨a city wall built entirely of earth.

When I first arrived there, I didn't know many people, and I often walked alone on the wall in the morning, strolling for dozens of spans, or even staying for half a day. The ground above was covered with velvety grass, facing the sunlight, all flourishing. In the middle of them, a small path that seemed hidden and only enough for one person to walk on was left out, and I roamed on it. Sometimes I looked up at the sky, and in the green sky, white clouds flew lazily over my head; sometimes I looked down at my feet... to see if any grass had been trampled by me, and the little butterflies flying among them all circled around me, as if surprised by this stranger who did not often come here. I also cast my long gaze into the distance, and saw an endless green wheat field, undulating with the wind, rolling towards me like the waves of the sea. Ah! A gust of wind blew open my heart. I walked forward, and after a few dozen steps, a row of willow trees came into view... some of the tree trunks were already very thick, and some were still slender. The hanging willow leaves made me think that comparing them to the waists of beauties was so disgusting. Ah! You criminals who specialize in stealing from nature! You have defiled nature! 丨I am extremely happy! I really doubt that this is not the human world. 丨Why doubt it? This is originally heaven!

I love willow trees the most, so I love to go even more to the place where willow trees are planted next to the earthen wall. I remember that one afternoon in summer, I met Fen near there, because there was a very large and deep pond right next to the wall, and she was driving a flock of ducks there to forage. The ducks were walking in front, waddling, and she was raising her hands behind them, following them while making a "shush shush" sound in her mouth. Heavens! I really don't know how to describe the scene at that time! It was really too wonderful!

She ran onto the wall, precisely where the willow trees were planted. 丨I should thank heaven that she, like me, also loves willow trees. She sat down under the shade of a willow tree, and I also went up and down, hearing good words丨How can I repeat it all? Rigid words can no longer express even a fraction of the vividness of the spirit at that time. She said that willow trees best suited her, that she liked the scenery of this temple the most, and that every time she came here to let the ducks out, she always had to come up and sit for a while. She had so much to say! Every time she switched from one sentence to another, she would always change to the most appropriate and natural expression. She said... "I have asked myself several times, 'Why does my heart feel so at peace every time I step onto this wall?'"

Everything about that earthen wall is now floating in front of my eyes again. Don't be angry, heaven, Miss Fen! The leaves of the willow trees should be hanging again!

Is Marriage the Tomb of Love? (Part 2) 271

— Xin Jie

Moreover, we also know that marriage is only a form. It only came into being after a certain kind of social system developed. Its essence is still the inevitable and reasonable demand between men and women. Its essence does not change because of the form of marriage. It's just that some colors have been embellished on the form. In primitive human society, when there was no surplus labor, everyone sought their own living materials by their own labor. The union between men and women was purely a reasonable union. There was no such chaotic and painful tragedy after marriage as in modern society. These are obvious facts.

Moreover, is the marriage life in modern society completely so miserable? It is not always the case. There are also relatively happy marriages. Moreover, there are some facts! After marriage, they love each other more than when they were in love. This is undoubtedly a part of the truth, and no one can deny it. So the problem is that marriage is certainly not the tomb of love, but a bad social structure gives marriage pain. However, we cannot therefore deny that marriage itself is reasonable, and negatively say that marriage is the tomb of love. At the same time, we are not like Ms. Ruizhu, saying that a sincere heart and unconditional love can solve the bad problems after marriage in modern society. Because the reason for the unreasonable result is not in the shift of each individual's subjective consciousness, it can be helpful, but it is; the factor is hidden in the bottom of the basic structure of society. Therefore, no matter how kind you are to shout that we should not use money and honor as the standard for combination, but in fact, as long as capitalist society exists for one day, and a new rational society does not appear for one day, there will always be many standards for combination based on money and honor. Moreover, it will further promote its poisonous tongue with the struggle of the dying capitalism of the dying years, so I said above that Ms. Ruizhu only sees the surface of the phenomenon, but fails to find the root of the problem, and only has a piece of kind advice.

Therefore, our conclusion is... finding the root cause of this problem is to solve it by reforming the basic structure of society. If the social system can be moved to a reasonable foundation, then marriage and love will not be contradictory, but will become generally reasonable, and further develop its reasonable self. Getting married not only does not make the passionate love of the past disappear, but also opens up more happy flowers and fruits. Returning to the original state of love and marriage that is without contradictions and without sin.

Biography of a Street Urchin (14) 272

— Chen Jingsheng

The general's authority is to make a person die if he wants to die, and to make a person live if he wants to live. But Lili told the general that... The braid is gone, what party will people point me to?

Not Lending to Chinese People 273

— Lvyun

It is not easy to live in Shanghai, and everyone knows that the rent reduction movement is not effective. A small clerk with a monthly salary of twenty or thirty yuan probably has to spend one-half or one-third of his total income on rent. In this way, renting a small house (a small area house) is the most difficult; is it the easiest thing for wealthy families who want to rent a large Western-style house? The day before yesterday, my friend and I went to the western district of Shanghai to look for houses along the street. Although there were very good buildings, they were either poorly lit or simply unsuitable for residential use. Finally, at the western end of Maiersi Avenue, we found a Tolet Western-style house. When we walked up to it, a foreman-like person shook his head and said that this place is not lent to Chinese people! He looked like a clown in a movie, with an unwilling look on his face. He also spoke the three words "Chinese people" with special effort; however, he himself, like us, is a Chinese of the Yellow race!

Foreigners built houses on our Chinese land, and they put on a stern face and said that they would not lend them to Chinese people. The reason, of course, is that Chinese people are a barbaric nation. As long as Chinese people arrive at any public place, they will make a mess of it. The previous sign at the park gate "Dogs and Chinese are not allowed" is also for this reason. Thinking about it, we Chinese are really hopeless. Now we are still being looked down upon in our own country. It is natural that there is a possibility of being forced to return home when studying abroad. What's there to say? There are also those like the foreman who help the evildoers.

Hot Wind (6) 274

— Cai Tonghua

(Note)

"Grandpa Bei said that this year is a year of disaster, famine, plague, alas! May the Bodhisattva bless us!" Old Grandma Jixiang muttered like chanting a mantra, covering her red, rotten, and blurry eyes with her sleeves.

"To hell with him, if it were me, I would have lost it long ago. Is it worth making such a fuss!"

"A Gen! May I ask how big your backer is? Lose it, your mother's old butt is not even smelly enough to stick candles in! You little devil."

Uncle Jia laughed wildly to himself, and the adults also laughed, and the children also laughed. The sound of laughter rippled in the space. A Xiang's face showed embarrassment and discomfort. He wanted to argue with Uncle Jia, but finally he held back. The children took the opportunity to squeeze into the middle, opened their eyes, sniffed their noses, and curiously looked at the faces of the adults.

"Where's Uncle Shunxing?"

"A Gua's father went to Mr. Yunfu to ask for help from Feng Bo." Shunxing's wife was both anxious and resentful. A Xing realized at this time that Uncle Shunxing was really not around.

"Asking the iron calculator for help, the ending is predictable..." Old Grandma Jixiang secretly pulled on Old Grandpa Jixiang's clothes, and Old Grandpa Jixiang's words were interrupted. Old Grandma Jixiang looked at everyone in a panic.

"Shunxing was too stubborn last year. He didn't sell the field to him, but now he asks him for help. He deserves this suffering, but if he doesn't ask him for help, there's no way." Someone in the crowd said this. Really, Mr. Yunfu was angry about this last year, and everyone knew it, and they were worried about Uncle Shunxing!

"Here he comes, here he comes;..."

The owner came, and the onlookers seemed to feel relieved, and their curiosity rose again. Everyone automatically dispersed. In addition to Uncle Shunxing and Feng Bo, he also brought a polite, smoothly haired, wearing a white gauze shirt and black trousers, and walking a bit like gentlemen, slowly swaying his figure-eight gait, and raising and lowering his shoulders, a small white face, and some people could recognize him, this was Mr. Yunfu's trusted servant. Shunxing's wife no longer had her eyebrows furrowed. Although Shunxing's resentful silence made her know that he had been wronged, she was relieved that Mr. Yunfu was willing to send someone. Because of the seriousness of the owner, they stood silently without any movement. The air suddenly became tense, and many eyes were focused on these three important characters who had just arrived.

"Brother Liu! You've worked hard." Feng Bo bowed humbly, and Shunxing also accompanied him, smiling bitterly. The guy who was called Brother Liu had an attitude as solemn as a priest in a church. He tucked those treasures under his armpits, and walked with arrogance. Feng Bo kept bowing and nodding, always seeing him off.

"May the gods and Buddhas bless us!" Shunxing's wife exhaled, a stone fell to the ground; the onlookers also exhaled in relief.

"Ten silver dollars in one hug, damn it!" Uncle Shunxing cursed angrily, shaking his head.

"Ten white dragons?" Shunxing's wife's small eyes were widened by this number, and the tears she had been holding back rolled down, and her face turned white.

"Money breaks through to bring peace! Money breaks through to bring peace!" Feng Bo waved his right hand, consoling miserably.

"Heavens, aren't twenty loads of sweet potatoes afraid of not selling for ten silver dollars!"

"Shunxing is too stupid, giving him two farts!"

"Hum! He wanted twenty yuan, but Brother Feng bitterly begged, damn it, that situation really made people angry to death!" Uncle Shunxing gritted his teeth and hated, Feng Bo smiled miserably.
